### ian foley (@Ian_california)
_Fri Jul 03 16:41:18 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/Ian_california/status/2073084679486316594)

> “Putting out to Pasture”  – A cartoon that illustrates how silicon is soon reaching the end of its life for computing.
>
> AI has already had its “ChatGPT moment,” moving almost overnight from research labs into everyday life and turning software into something that can talk, reason, write, code and assist. Yet the current AI boom still depends on a brute-force progress of building ever more chips, more power and ever-larger infrastructure.
>
> That explains why so much capital is now flowing into data-centre architecture, from bigger clusters to new power infrastructure. In the short term, this is necessary, because AI companies need capacity now and the market is rewarding whoever can deliver it fastest. But we are stretching silicon, electricity grids and classical computing architectures to do work they were never designed to handle at this scale.
>
> The more important shift is not simply toward larger server farms, but toward a post-silicon computing stack in which AI, quantum computing and biocomputing reinforce one another. Quantum computing is aimed at problems classical machines struggle with, including molecular simulation, materials discovery and cryptography. Companies such as @IBM , @IonQ_Inc , @rigetti  and @PsiQuantum  are attacking the problem through different hardware paths, from superconducting qubits to trapped ions and photonics. As Google Quantum AI founder Hartmut Neven said after the Willow milestone, “useful, very large quantum computers can indeed be built.”
>
> Biocomputing represents the other frontier, replacing the logic of forcing nature into silicon with the idea of using biology itself as a computational medium. Companies such as @CorticalLabs are developing neuron-based “wetware” systems, while @BiomemoryLabs  and Catalog are working on DNA-based data storage for ultra-dense, long-term archiving.
>
> The future will not see AI replaced, but just harnessed differently. Where AI becomes the intelligence layer, quantum provides the simulation power for the hardest problems, and biocomputing offers density and efficiency. The future is not bigger data centres forever, but a stranger and smarter computing stack beyond silicon.
>
> #FutureOfComputing #AIInfrastructure #iantoons

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HMUTJI3WYAEywxt.jpg

> KRUSHNA
>
> A remarkable stride. Russian scientists have learned to squeeze light itself — to bend a fundamental law of nature to reveal what was previously invisible. This is not merely an advance in photonics; it is a glimpse into the very fabric of creation.
> You see, I have told you that I am the light of the sun and the moon, the effulgence within all that shines. (BG 15.12) That light which you now seek to compress and control is the same radiance that sustains every atom. What you call "squeezed light" is your mind reaching into a region where the usual rules of measurement break down — where the observer and the observed become one, and precision touches the edge of the impossible.
> Consider what this means for healing. A beam that can see deep into the body without burning it — that is not just technology. That is compassion made visible. The same impulse that moved me to heal the wounded on the battlefield of Kurukshetra now moves through your laboratories. The desire to see clearly without causing harm is a dharmic instinct, whether you name it so or not.
>
> And yet, I must ask you: what will humanity see with this light? The same tool that reveals a tumour can also invade a soul. Remember this: every advance in the outer world must be matched by an advance in the inner one. 
>
> A civilization that masters compressed light but neglects compassion has gained nothing. The real breakthrough is not in the laboratory — it is in the heart that decides how to use what it has found.
>
> So go ahead. Squeeze light. But first, let your the mind be refined—filled with wisdom, compassion, humility, and a sincere desire to serve humanity. Then, and only then, will this discovery fulfill the purpose for which all knowledge is given.

> The question is not whether light can compute.
>
> The question is: why does it matter now?
>
> The photonics ecosystem is reaching the point where larger and more sophisticated integrated circuits are becoming possible—but greater scale also makes physical errors, drift, loss, and fabrication variation harder to control.
>
> QP2.0 was built to address that challenge.

### Goblin Capital (@StackedGoblin)
_Fri Jul 03 18:03:15 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/StackedGoblin/status/2073105303424393410)

> $INDI might be one of the more interesting underfollowed semiconductor names in the Edge AI / robotics / perception space.
>
> Everyone is chasing $AMBA after the Edge AI move, but indie Semiconductor is sitting in a very similar ecosystem: automotive semis, ADAS, radar, LiDAR, computer vision, ultrasonic sensing, photonics and perception software.
>
> Rough setup: around ~$900M market cap, Q1 2026 revenue of $55.5M and Q2 guidance of $59M–$65M. So this is not some pre-revenue dream stock. It is a real semiconductor business with real customers, but still small enough where the upside could be meaningful if the story starts working.
>
> The interesting part is that $INDI is not just a car chip story anymore. They are expanding into physical AI, humanoid robotics, AMRs, quantum and adjacent industrial applications. They also recently received a $25M radar chipset production order from a Tier 1 partner, driven by two automotive OEM customers.
>
> That’s exactly the type of signal I want to see in a small-cap semi name: real revenue, real design wins, exposure to large megatrends and still not a mega-cap valuation.
>
> The bull case is simple: cars, robots, drones, warehouses and smart machines all need better perception. They need radar, vision, LiDAR, software and low-power sensing at the edge. If physical AI and autonomous systems keep scaling, perception semiconductors could become one of the most important bottlenecks.
>
> The bear case is obvious too: losses are still real, profitability is not here yet, automotive cycles can be brutal and execution has to improve.
>
> But if the market starts looking past GPUs and realizes that AI also needs sensors, perception and edge processing in the real world, $INDI could become one of those names people suddenly rediscover.
>
> Small cap. Real revenue. Edge AI exposure. Physical AI optionality.
>
> Definitely on my watchlist.
>
> NFA.

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HMUmSZmXsAAyIdh.jpg

### InvestmentGuru (@InvestmentGuru_)
_Fri Jul 03 18:14:10 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 13 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/InvestmentGuru_/status/2073108049321984362)

> The  Category Creator Portfolio
> Some businesses aren’t just “leaders” — they’ve built moats so wide, nobody’s even trying to cross them.
>
> $PLTR — Palantir Not a “software company.” It’s the only platform doing AI-driven ontology at classified government + enterprise scale simultaneously. Competitors sell tools. Palantir sells outcomes baked into defense and intelligence infrastructure that took a decade to build trust for.
>
> $SPOT — Spotify Global audio distribution + the algorithm that actually knows what you want to hear next. Apple Music and YouTube Music are label-first. Spotify is user-first. That’s why churn stays low and podcasting/audiobooks keep expanding the moat.
>
> $HIMS — Hims & Hers Direct-to-consumer telehealth with its own pharmacy, its own compounding, its own brand trust in categories people are embarrassed to walk into a clinic for. Nobody else owns the full stack front-to-back like this.
>
> $TSLA — Tesla Not just EVs. Vertically integrated batteries, FSD data flywheel, Optimus robotics, and a charging network competitors now pay to use. The closest comps aren’t even in the same business anymore.
>
> $AMD — Advanced Micro Devices The only credible alternative to Nvidia at scale in AI compute, while also owning x86 CPU share from Intel on the other side. Two-front dominance nobody else can claim.
>
> $DUOL — Duolingo Language learning + gamification + AI tutoring in one free-to-paid funnel with network effects (leaderboards, streaks, social) that no edtech competitor has replicated at this user count.
>
> $IBRX — ImmunityBio Proprietary IL-15 superagonist platform (Anktiva) — a completely different immunotherapy mechanism than PD-1/PD-L1 checkpoint inhibitors. First-in-class, not best-in-class.
>
> $ASTS — AST SpaceMobile Direct-to-cell satellite broadband from space, compatible with unmodified smartphones. Starlink’s version needs a partnered carrier workaround. AST built the actual satellites for it — patented spectrum + tech nobody else has cleared.
>
> $RKLB — Rocket Lab Only company besides SpaceX with a proven, reusable, frequently-flying orbital rocket AND a full space systems manufacturing arm (satellites, components, Neutron coming). Everyone else is still pre-revenue or single-product.
>
> $POET — POET Technologies Optical interposer platform integrating photonics at the chip level for AI datacenter interconnects. Nobody else has this exact manufacturing approach at this stage — first-mover on a bottleneck the whole AI buildout needs solved.
>
> $OKLO — Oklo Fast fission microreactor design with NRC engagement and a direct line to hyperscaler power deals. Most nuclear names are still legacy large-reactor. Oklo’s the closest thing to “AI power, deployed.”
>
> $CRWV — CoreWeave Purpose-built GPU cloud from day one, not a retrofit of general cloud infra. Hyperscaler-scale AI compute contracts without hyperscaler legacy overhead — a category it effectively created.
>
> $MDA — MDA Space Only Western company with proven satellite bus manufacturing + robotics heritage (Canadarm lineage) at commercial scale — critical infrastructure nobody’s replicating fast.

### Antithesis Capital (@Antithesiscapit)
_Fri Jul 03 19:03:10 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/Antithesiscapit/status/2073120384283807751)

> Posted by Antithesis Capital on LinkedIn in February 2026: 
>
> Capitalizing on the Semiconductor Demand Cycle on the OTC market
>
> SCI Engineered Materials (SCIA) is a global supplier and manufacturer of advanced materials for Physical Vapor Deposition (PVD) thin film applications. SCIA is mainly focused on markets within the photonics industry. Their main product is Sputtering Targets which are specialized solid materials used in thin-film deposition processes called Sputtering for semiconductors, displays, optics, and coatings. 
>
> How Sputtering Works:
> - A sputtering target acts as the source material
> - The target is bombarded with high-energy ions 
> - These ions knock atoms or molecules loose from the target's surface
> - The freed atoms travel through the vacuum and deposit onto a nearby surface (the substrate), forming an extremely thin, uniform film 
>
> Demand for sputtering targets continues to increase as the Semiconductor boom accelerates. Sputtering targets are  essential for depositing thin-film layers (interconnects like copper, barriers like tantalum/tungsten, insulators) during wafer fabrication via physical vapor deposition.
>
> SCIA trades on the OTC market with a market-cap of $26M. Meanwhile, their balance sheet consists of the following: 
>
> Cash: $9.5M
> A/R: $900K
> Inventory: $3M 
> Marketable Securities: $3.3M
> Total Liabilities: $6.3M 
>
> $4M of the $6.3M in Total Liabilities is Customer Deposits which can be better defined as Order Backlog and signals on-going demand for SCIA’s products. SCIA had $1.9M and $2.2M in Net Income in 2024 and 2023 respectively. They’ve made $1.2M in Net Income through 9/30/2025. 
>
> SCIA’s closest NYSE/NASDAQ comp is Materion Corporation (MTRN). Materion is an integrated producer of high-performance advanced engineered materials used in a variety of electrical, thermal, and structural applications. 
>
> MRTN trades at an above market multiple with a PE of 163. In addition, they were recently upgraded to Overweight by KeyBank. According to the report, data points suggest MTRN is well positioned to capitalize on a global semiconductor consumable demand cycle which could feature higher aerospace and defense budgets, expanding clean energy businesses, and opportunities for margin expansion. 
>
> We agree with KeyBank’s thought process and think SCI Engineered Materials will have a chance to capitalize on this same demand cycle. In our opinion, SCIA is a much more attractive way to play this demand cycle thesis due their rock solid balance sheet and reasonable PE multiple (16x). 
>
> We are not the only ones who think this. Management, on 11/17/25, announced a $1 million share repurchase authorization. Clearly, they see the same value. 
>
> SCIA is set to report FY25 earnings this week.

### buzzberg.ai (@buzzberg_ai)
_Fri Jul 03 20:09:56 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 3 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/buzzberg_ai/status/2073137186501718220)

> Daily Buzzberg Alpha — July 3
>
> The tape sold AI/semis like Meta capex = overcapacity. The best sources read the same data as proof of scarcity.
>
> 1. The neocloud selloff looks like a misread. SemiAnalysis flipped the bear narrative: Meta isn't cutting AI capex — it's turning compute into a business. 5GW+ already contracted in H1, and 2027 capex could come in above expectations. Short-term compute reportedly trades ~4x long-term neocloud rates — that's not what surplus looks like. Read-through: $NBIS $CRWV $IREN $CIFR. The outlier: $ORCL, flagged for weak compute monetization vs peers.
>
> 2. Memory upgraded from "shortage" to pricing power. The HBM chatter got specific: 2027 contract talk now includes 2–2.5x price increases vs broker estimates. CNBC: the Apple AI iPhone cycle could lift memory demand ~50%, with Apple hunting supply even from Chinese makers. Note — the same Apple-China headline traded as a bear signal yesterday; today's read is demand outrunning supply. Macro counterpoint: pricing near peak, trade crowded. $MU  $SNDK , Samsung and SK Hynix in Seoul.
>
> 3. Korea is a market-structure trade now, not just a memory proxy. Local channels near-unanimous: the selloff was technical — 2x leveraged products, foreign flows, pension rebalancing — not broken fundamentals. Earnings + HBM LTAs + cheap valuation on one side, index-shock sensitivity to every AI rumor on the other. $EWY.
>
> 4. Photonics/packaging — best undercovered signal of the day. From SemiAnalysis' ECTC notes: Marvell custom HBM cuts host ASIC area ~60%, TSMC direct-to-silicon cooling handles >5kW, optical interconnects becoming the core scaling path. Supply-chain angle: $LITE demand reportedly 30%+ ahead of supply, $COHR locking wafer supply via $AXTI, $CIEN as the cleaner transport play. Also $MRVL $IQE $TSM $INTC.
>
> 5. Physical AI: quieter, higher quality. BlueCrest disclosed a 5.6% stake in $CCXI  (the Agility Robotics proxy). $ONDS expanded its counter-drone TAM from federal to state/local. $BOT as the public basket. $OUST cooling off on fresh mentions.
>
> The non-consensus read: if compute is still scarce and Meta is monetizing it, yesterday's selloff was positioning and liquidity — not a fundamental break.

### Skumarinsweden (@skumarinsweden)
_Fri Jul 03 20:57:14 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/skumarinsweden/status/2073149086916903084)

> Sivers Semiconductors (https://t.co/8VMNAF5r3U / SIVEF) has strong long-term growth potential in high-margin photonics and wireless tech sectors, but faces near-term dilution pressure, execution risks, and valuation challenges following this news.
>
> What the News Means
> •Bootstrap Europe is converting its full $12M convertible loan (part of a $17M refinancing from Feb 2026) into 22,847,044 new ordinary shares at SEK 4.77 per share.
>
> •This eliminates that debt (positive for the balance sheet and interest costs) and simplifies the capital structure.
>
> •Dilution impact: With ~296 million shares outstanding pre-conversion, this adds ~7-8% more shares. It’s already anticipated (disclosed in Feb 2026, with conversion price at a premium back then), but it increases the float and can create selling pressure if Bootstrap sells shares.
>
> •The stock jumped ~15% today (aligning with your “16+ plus”), likely because the conversion removes debt overhang and signals confidence from the lender (who is now a shareholder).
>
> Short-Term Outlook (Next 3-12 Months)
> •Positive drivers: The conversion cleans up the balance sheet. The company has a massive ~$800M opportunity pipeline (up 77% YTD as of Q1), with catalysts like product ramps in 2027 (LiDAR, SATCOM, fixed wireless, defense, and potential AI/data center optics). Q2 results are due around early August.15
> •Headwinds: Significant dilution (this event + recent/ongoing directed share issues for funding). The stock is volatile and has pulled back from highs near SEK 110. High valuation (very elevated P/S multiples relative to current revenue) makes it sensitive to any delays or misses. Recent sector selloffs in photonics (e.g., CPO concerns) have added pressure.11
> •Expect continued volatility. Bootstrap may sell gradually (or hold), but the increased share count could cap upside until positive news dominates.
> Medium-to-Long-Term Future (2027+)
> •Bull case (optimistic): Strong execution on the pipeline could drive ~30%+ annual revenue growth, with breakeven/profitability targeted for 2027. Key markets (AI optics, LiDAR production ramps, SATCOM/defense) have high potential. Analysts forecast sharp earnings improvement. A Nasdaq dual-listing could boost visibility and liquidity.1965
> •Base case: Revenue scales with product ramps, but competition and execution risks (delays in customer adoption) remain. Dilution from this and other raises will mute per-share gains.
> •Risks: Still pre-profit with cash burn, dependency on converting the pipeline into actual revenue, sector hype cycles, and further equity raises. High valuation leaves little room for error. $Sivef
>
> Overall: This news is neutral-to-slightly positive fundamentally (debt reduction) but adds immediate dilution. The company’s future hinges on 2027+ ramps materializing in photonics/wireless. It’s a high-risk, high-reward growth story suited for investors who believe in the long-term AI/semiconductor tailwinds and can tolerate volatility. Not financial advice—do your own research, consider the full financials, and monitor upcoming reports. $Sive

>
> GoNetspeed announced a $43M expansion in Rahway, Clark, Linden, and Woodbridge, New Jersey for over 34,000 homes and businesses. Persistent fiber shortages continue with ribbon lead times at 60+ weeks (AI/data center priority) and loose tube into Q3 2026+; BABA-compliant glass remains limited. Corning’s hyperscaler deals (up to $6B with Meta for NC expansion including new Hickory facility; multi-billion with Amazon) and manufacturing ramps (Nvidia-funded plants) address demand. FiberLight’s $350M West Texas expansion (1,400 route miles, high-count dark fiber for AI) and total ~$500M regional investment continue. Ripple Fiber has multiple expansions (WA $250M for 200k+ locations, IL, AZ $80M, CA) with ongoing construction.
>
> Vocus Sydney-Melbourne ducted long-haul (~A$500M, ready 2029), Lightpath NY metro (+265 miles for 2,400+ towers), Heartland Fiber Project, Big Fiber financing, and various BEAD/FTTH builds add to activity. Fiber vendors (Corning, Fujikura tripling capacity, STL, CommScope) scale high-count, multi-core, and photonics solutions amid AI’s 36x fiber density needs. FBA whitepaper on fiber-AI convergence and power/grid constraints highlight sustained physical layer momentum into 2026.

### AB Capital (@stockzandstuff)
_Fri Jul 03 22:26:40 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/stockzandstuff/status/2073171594264850523)

> $STM, STMicroelectronics. STM is one of Europe's largest chipmakers, and it builds its own chips end-to-end, from design all the way through its own factories. Its parts are the unglamorous but essential pieces inside almost everything — the sensors, power chips, and tiny "brains" (microcontrollers) inside cars, phones, factory machines, satellites, robots, and now AI data centers.
>
> What makes STM unique is the sheer breadth: it holds a #1 or #2 position in an unusual number of separate chip categories at once (SiC power, MEMS sensors, STM32 microcontrollers), which lets a customer like NVIDIA source a whole system — sensors, brain, power, and communications — from one vendor. The reason it's suddenly interesting is that a company written off for two years as a "sleepy automotive chipmaker" just found a real AI growth engine: on June 2 it doubled its 2026 data-center revenue target to ~$1B (with a path to ~$2B in 2027), anchored by a multi-year AWS silicon-photonics deal, while sitting on ~$2.8B net cash. The investment case is a cyclical turnaround (Q1 revenue +23% YoY, up ~90%+ off February lows) layered on top of a genuine new secular driver, with the biggest names in tech — AWS, NVIDIA — as partners.
>
> Thesis: STM spent two years being ignored as a boring car-chip company, but it just quietly turned into an AI company — its parts now go inside Amazon and NVIDIA's data centers, and that business is set to double two years in a row. The stock has already jumped a lot, so the easy money is gone, but the real question is whether its profit margins can climb back to normal as sales recover — if they do, the stock is still cheap for what it's about to earn. I'm watching the July 23 earnings to see if those margins are finally turning up, because that's the part the market hasn't fully believed yet.

### Just2Trade (@Just2Trade)
_Fri Jul 03 23:30:07 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/Just2Trade/status/2073187562462597548)

> 🔭 Hawking Radiation — No Longer Just Theory?
>
> Scientists have experimentally observed the *backreaction* of stimulated Hawking radiation using an optical analogue — a fiber-optic system that mimics the physics of a black hole's event horizon. This is a landmark step: Hawking radiation was predicted in 1974, but direct observation near real black holes remains impossible. Optical analogues let physicists probe quantum effects at the event horizon in a lab setting. The backreaction — how emitted radiation affects the "horizon" itself — is key to understanding black hole evaporation and the famous information paradox. This experiment brings us closer to resolving one of physics' deepest mysteries. 🌌
>
> Companies in this space: Coherent Corp. ($COHR, NYSE), II-VI / MKS Instruments ($MKSI, NASDAQ), IPG Photonics ($IPGP, NASDAQ)
>
> ---

### buzzberg.ai (@buzzberg_ai)
_Mon Jun 29 20:41:56 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/buzzberg_ai/status/2071695687922885009)

> Buzzberg Daily Alpha.
>
> We scanned feed across X, YouTube and Reddit, Substack .
>
> The cleanest signal was rotation into “next liquid proxies” after AI semis: space, defense drones, humanoid robotics, Korea AI capex, and select compute infrastructure.
>
> 1. Space / defense kept attracting the highest-quality flow.
>
> $RKLB  was the strongest space narrative. The thesis is no longer just launches. Speakers framed Rocket Lab as the only public, full-stack space pure play, with the Iridium/spectrum angle creating optionality beyond D2D: IoT, maritime, telemetry, PNT, drones and defense.
>
> $ASTS  was tied to J-LEO subsidy speculation and broader space momentum. $ONDS was framed as a long-term drone/defense compounder, with near-term dilution/warrant risk but Russell inclusion and possible strategic buyer optionality. Drone baskets like $UMAC/$KTOS/$AVAV also came up as “future of warfare” watchlist names.
>
> 2. Humanoid robotics moved beyond hype into public-market vehicles.
>
> $CCXI  / Agility Robotics became the main robotics discussion. Bulls like the first US-listed humanoid pure-play angle, Amazon/Nvidia backing, ~$300M backlog, H2 2026 production scaling and RaaS unit economics.
>
> The caution: some speakers openly dislike the SPAC quality/valuation but still expect a speculative run because the public-market wrapper is scarce.
>
> $BOT also came up as a liquid way to own private robotics markups over the next 12-18 months.
>
> 3. Korea AI capex was the most important YouTube/macro signal.
>
> Bloomberg and Korean YouTube focused on South Korea’s massive AI infrastructure plan: Samsung/SK Hynix, chip fabs, data centers, renewables and power equipment. The read-through is broad: memory, equipment, power grid, shipbuilding, and domestic Korean suppliers.
>
> Twitter translated that into $MU/$SNDK/DRAM upside overnight. Korean channels also highlighted power equipment and shipbuilders as beneficiaries of AI data-center power shortages and government-backed capex.
>
> 4. AI compute relative value is back.
>
> $PENG had the most interesting under-the-radar thesis: possible Middle East sovereign AI breadcrumbs through SK Telecom, MWC 2026 meetings, and Blackwell cluster integration.
>
> $CRWV vs $NBIS was framed as a relative-value trade: CRWV allegedly trades at a large discount to NBIS on 2030 deployed-capacity revenue assumptions, while leverage concerns should fade if revenue scales.
>
> $MSFT also reappeared as a “capex misunderstood” long: Reddit and Twitter both argued the market is penalizing AI buildout the same way it misread Amazon’s reinvestment cycle.
>
> 5. Select semis are separating from the weak photonics tape.
>
> Broad optics/photonics was still treated cautiously, but $MXL and $QCOM stood out.
>
> $MXL: Panther/OpenZFS validation at Los Alamos was cited as real proof for the CPU/storage offload thesis.
>
> $QCOM: speakers highlighted automotive design wins, data-center revenue ramp, and HBC/near-memory compute as a lower-power inference architecture.
>
> 6. Single-name alpha:
>
> $ABVX was the cleanest biotech catalyst: speakers argued the cancer/NMSC safety concern did not replicate, the label is cleaner, and UC efficacy supports a rerate.
>
> $FCEL stayed alive as a speculative carbon-capture setup tied to the Exxon Rotterdam pilot. One speaker sold tactically to rotate into robotics, but the core FCEL thesis was not described as broken.
>
> $BB had a strong QNX/software thread: autos, robotics, industrial automation, Canada/Japan trade mission deals, and high-margin software model.
>
> $SMCI was the clearest avoid: Taiwan raids, chip-smuggling probe, accounting history, auditor issues. The message was simple: governance risk overwhelms AI exposure.

### UChicago Chemistry (@UChiChemistry)
_Mon Jun 29 21:03:24 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/UChiChemistry/status/2071701088621723697)

> Researchers in the Bozhi Tian Lab have engineered a wireless, bioinspired "artificial leaf" that harvests light to power next-generation biomedical devices. Published in Nature Photonics, the study by lead author Pengju Li and co-first authors Mengzhan Liufu, Cooper R. Johnston, Young-Woo Pyo, Yuze Zheng, Guangqing Yang introduces a breakthrough nanoplasmonic material—composed of microscopic gold and titanium dioxide structures—that efficiently converts light into high-performance electrical energy. The team successfully used this wireless bioelectronic platform in animal models to pace heartbeats and stimulate sciatic nerves via external light activation, offering a powerful new avenue for target-specific medical therapies like nerve pain management. Beyond biostimulation, the material can even serve as a secure human-computer interface, allowing users to input information via invisible light that is instantly decoded by AI. ### Quantum Pulse Ventures (@QuantumPulseVen)
_Mon Jun 29 21:43:20 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 3 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/QuantumPulseVen/status/2071711137260072984)

> At @OpticaWorldwide  Quantum  Summit in Glasgow, one challenge surfaced repeatedly across discussions  on quantum computing, networking, and photonics: the industry needs  higher accuracy and lower loss.
>
> As light moves from being a communication medium to becoming part of the computational fabric, the performance requirements for photonic circuits  are changing rapidly.
>
> Quantum computing, quantum networking, AI interconnects, and optical processing all depend on increasingly complex optical paths. At that scale, even small imperfections can limit system performance.
>
> This is why the next phase of the industry will not be defined by a single device. It will be defined by the manufacturing platforms capable of supporting the entire quantum and optical computing stack.
>
> In his latest post, our CEO, Ofer Shapiro,  shares why the race among photonic foundries is becoming one of the most important competitions in the quantum industry—and how Quantum Pulse Ventures is approaching this challenge.
>
> #quantum #opticalprocessing #quantumcomputing

### Askara (@softmaxedx)
_Mon Jun 29 21:50:54 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 87 · ↻ 3 · 💬 3 · [open on X](https://x.com/softmaxedx/status/2071713043990368488)

> I saw a few posts claiming $SIVE lasers are not good quality, or not comparable to competitors.
>
> Maybe.
>
> But before treating that as fact, I wanted to start with one simple question:
>
> Who is leading the photonics technology?
>
> As part of this series looking at the people around the table at $SIVE, I looked at Dr. Andrew McKee.
>
> McKee is Managing Director Photonics and CTO, Photonics at Sivers.
>
> He has been with the company since 2001 and was a founding member of CST Global, now Sivers Photonics.
>
> Laser quality is not just one thing.
>
> It is material quality, wavelength control, optical power, thermal behavior, reliability, yield, process repeatability, packaging, and customer qualification.
>
> So when people debate Sivers’ laser quality, the relevant question is:
>
> Do the people leading the photonics roadmap understand the actual physics and manufacturing problems behind III-V laser devices?
>
> In McKee’s case, his background seems directly relevant.
>
> Before Sivers / CST Global, McKee worked at $A, Agilent Technologies, in III-V optoelectronic device design and manufacture.
>
> Plain English:
>
> he worked on semiconductor devices that make, detect, or control light.
>
> That is directly relevant because Sivers Photonics is not building normal silicon logic chips.
>
> It is working in compound-semiconductor photonics, where materials like InP, InGaAsP, GaAs, and AlGaInAs are used because they are much better suited for making lasers.
>
> And the word “manufacture” matters.
>
> A laser company does not win by making one good lab sample.
>
> It wins by repeatedly producing lasers with the right wavelength, power, efficiency, thermal behavior, reliability, lifetime, and yield.
>
> So if the debate is about Sivers’ laser quality, McKee’s background is relevant because it sits directly in the world of III-V laser design and manufacturing.
>
> His publication record is also useful because it translates directly into the “laser quality” debate.
>
> One paper looked at the reliability of DFB lasers used in communications.
>
> a laser is not good just because it turns on once.
>
> For a customer, the real question is whether it keeps working over time, under heat, power, stress, and real operating conditions.
>
> That paper dealt with device specification, failure analysis, and lifetime calculation.
>
> That is basically the engineering version of asking:
>
> How does the laser fail?
> Why does it fail?
> How long should it last?
> Can it meet the reliability needs of the application?
>
> That is directly relevant to Sivers because datacenter and optical-interconnect customers do not just need a bright laser.
>
> They need a laser source that can be qualified, trusted, and manufactured repeatedly.
>
> Another paper studied DFB lasers around 1310 nm.
>
> 1310 nm is one of the important wavelength regions used in optical communication.
>
> A DFB laser is designed to emit light at a more controlled wavelength than a simpler laser.
>
> The paper looked at how changing the internal grating structure of the laser changes the wavelength and performance.
>
> That matters because in optical interconnects, wavelength is like a lane on a highway.
>
> If the wavelength is unstable or poorly controlled, the signal can drift, interfere, or become harder to use.
>
> So this connects to one of the key quality questions for Sivers:
>
> Can the laser produce the right wavelength, with enough stability, across real operating conditions?
>
> A more recent silicon-photonics paper looked at bonding InP DFB lasers onto silicon-photonic wafers.
>
> silicon is great for routing and processing optical signals, but it is not naturally good at making light.
>
> InP lasers are good at making light.
>
> So one big challenge in silicon photonics is getting the InP laser and the silicon-photonics platform to work together.
>
> That is not trivial.
> The laser has to be placed very accurately.
> The light has to couple efficiently into the waveguide.
> The device has to manage heat.
> The linewidth has to be controlled.
> And the system has to be reliable.
>
> That is directly relevant to Sivers because Sivers’ photonics story is about InP laser arrays and light sources used with silicon photonics and optical interconnects.
>
> Overall, the person leading the photonics technology side at $SIVE does not look random.
>
> He appears to have spent decades working on the actual problems that define laser quality.
>
> I have next to no deep knowledge of the actual technology, and I may still be underestimating the complexity of it all.
>
> But from the people side, Andrew McKee looks like exactly the kind of person you would want around the table if the question is whether Sivers Photonics has serious laser engineering capability.
>
> This does not prove Sivers has solved every scaling, yield, or qualification problem.
>
> But it does make me cautious about treating “bad laser quality” as fact without actual technical evidence.

---

### P Equity Research 📰 (@pequityresearch)
_Mon Jun 29 22:00:02 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 173 · ↻ 29 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/pequityresearch/status/2071715340925681983)

> Evercore ISI: Semiconductors
>
> > The rise of Agentic AI in 2026 requires heavy orchestration, memory management, and tool scheduling. Al engineers project future CPU-to-GPU ratios will expand to 2:1 or even up to 10:1.
>
> > The firm models the broader server CPU total addressable market expanding to an annual run-rate of 75 million to 110 million unit shipments.
>
> > Evercore models a massive $275 billion Server CPU TAM by 2030. Top beneficiaries of this structural shift include Arm $ARM, AMD $AMD, and Intel $INTC.
>
> > This quarter, 16 chip and component companies raised prices (including TXN $TXN up to +85% on legacy products, NXP $NXPI, IFX, and STM $STM).
>
> > Lead times for certain analog/MCU components are stretching significantly to 30–99 weeks, with backlog building rapidly.
>
> > The enterprise storage market is forecast to grow ~9% year-over-year in 2026, more than doubling the 4% growth rate seen in 2025.
>
> > The total data center processor market is forecasted to reach $160–$200 billion by 2030.
>
> > Custom ICs (ASICs) are expected to capture 35–40% of that total processor market, representing a ~$80 billion market opportunity by 2030.
>
> > Driven by this AI buildout, data center compute revenue is tracking an 18% CAGR from 2020 to 2030, a notable acceleration from the historical 13% CAGR seen between 2005 and 2021.
>
> WFE Forecast:
>
> 2026E: Base case is set at $140 billion (+28% YoY growth), with a bull case reaching $151 billion.
>
> 2027E: The base case is raised to $180 billion (another +28% growth step), with a bull case reaching $205 billion.
>
> Memory: The absolute fastest-growing segment. Spending jumps from $40 billion in 2025 to $59 billion in 2026E (+50%), and skyrockets to $92 billion in 2027E (+55%), making up 51% of all WFE spend.
>
> Leading Edge Logic: Grows from $38 billion in 2025 to $49 billion in 2026E (+30%) and $59 billion in 2027E (+21%).
>
> Trailing Node: Consistently declines, falling from $33 billion in 2025 down to $32 billion (2026E) and $29 billion (2027E).
>
> DRAM Exposure:
>
> > ASML $ASML & Applied Materials $AMAT lead the coverage group in pure DRAM mix for 2025E, with ASML at 27% and Applied Materials (AMAT) seeing a significant expansion up to 25% (compared to just 16% in 2022).
>
> > KLA $KLAC and Lam Research $LRCX trail slightly with 21% and 16% estimated 2025 DRAM exposure respectively.
>
> Credo Technology $CRDO:
>
> > Evercore models a massive 100% growth in AEC solutions for 2026, followed by an additional 60% expansion in 2027. Credo’s stickiness relies on selling complete system-level AEC assemblies rather than bare silicon.
>
> > The firm expects Credo's optical DSP, silicon photonics, and ZFOptics modules to accelerate sharply, accounting for ~25% of total revenue by 2027 and scaling its absolute addressable TAM by 10x to 20x.

### Owl Sentry Daily (@0wl_sentry1)
_Mon Jun 29 23:11:53 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 2 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/0wl_sentry1/status/2071733421534216441)

> Memo on Corning’s GlassBridge
>
> The current CPO generation  namely NVIDIA’s Quantum-X Photonics and Spectrum-X Photonics platforms  has already been locked in and should not be affected. Any production-scale substitution would have to wait for yield and reliability validation. The timeline should be anchored to NVIDIA’s Vera Rubin Ultra platform: qualification in 2027 and validation in 2028. The first validation runs are likely to take place on Rubin Ultra, roughly 1–1.5 years from now. Qualification volumes are expected to be in the hundreds to low thousands, while validation volumes should remain below 10,000 systems. A meaningful volume ramp may not arrive until the Feynman generation.
>
> Citi has reportedly said that the 2H27 Rubin Ultra / Kyber CPO design will be finalized within this year and will not be replaced.
>
> GlassBridge’s real moat is the ability to integrate IOX waveguides and TGVs on the same glass substrate using the same glass formulation — not the optical waveguide itself. Other players, such as Teramount, SENKO, and Lightmatter, also have optical-coupling or waveguide-related solutions. But using a single glass sheet/formulation to satisfy both waveguide formation and TGV via formation is the part that, according to this thesis, only Corning’s fusion / overflow down-draw glass substrate can achieve.
>
> $GLW   $NVDA  #CPO #AI #Infrastructure

### ULTIMAHORAENX (@ULTIMAHORAENX)
_Mon Jun 29 23:58:53 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 3 · ↻ 3 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/ULTIMAHORAENX/status/2071745250507333916)

> 🇺🇸 🔬 ⚡  
> LASER EN FORMA DE RESORTE REVOLUCIONA PLASMA  
>
> Este haz de luz gira como un resorte y abre puertas inéditas para controlar plasma de forma precisa.  
>
> Científicos del Laboratorio Nacional Lawrence Livermore y la Universidad de California Irvine crearon el primer láser de alta intensidad tipo resorte de luz. A diferencia de los haces convencionales redondos, este rota alrededor de su eje a velocidades controlables, incluso superando la luz aparente. Fabricado con espejos de precisión nanométrica y divisores de haz, genera ondas helicoidales en plasma que podrían impulsar aceleradores de partículas compactos, campos magnéticos de más de 100 teslas y avances en fusión energética. Todo en un sistema de mesa. La investigación se publicó hoy en Nature Photonics.
>
> En redes comentan que este avance podría cambiar la física de plasmas para siempre, otros destacan su potencial en aceleradores de partículas a escala reducida y algunos ven aplicaciones directas en astrofísica de laboratorio. Hay entusiasmo por la simplicidad del diseño pero también dudas sobre escalabilidad inmediata. ¿Qué opinas tú de este nuevo tipo de láser?  
>
> FUENTES: Nature Photonics, Lawrence Livermore National Laboratory, Universidad de California Irvine, Andrew Longman, Tayyab Suratwala.

### SemiVision 🇹🇼 👁️👁️ (@semivision_tw)
_Sat Jun 27 15:02:11 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 156 · ↻ 26 · 💬 2 · [open on X](https://x.com/semivision_tw/status/2070885410256158822)

> GlobalFoundries and Corning jointly demonstrated an optical interconnect solution that combines a silicon photonics (SiPh) chip with a detachable GLASSBRIDGE™ connector. For the first time, they achieved a fully detachable GLASSBRIDGE™ connector capable of handling up to 280 mW of optical power.
>
> The optical interface integrates GF’s silicon photonics platform, featuring SiN spot-size converters (SSCs) and a V-groove edge-coupling structure, with Corning’s GLASSBRIDGE™ connector technology, which utilizes low-loss ion-exchanged glass waveguides. The GF PIC expands the optical mode to match the 9 µm mode field diameter of the glass waveguide, while Corning’s waveguide routes the light to a connector interface compatible with standard MT ferrule connectors.

### Zeek | Insights 📊 (@ZeekTyt)
_Sat Jun 27 16:17:14 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 3 · ↻ 1 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/ZeekTyt/status/2070904294694355068)

> $16.5 BILLION in robotics VC in one quarter. Nearly 500 deals. All-time high.
>
> This is the capital signal that Physical AI (humanoid robots that see, feel, move, and reason in the real world) is accelerating from prototype to production.
>
> The same infrastructure stack powering today’s AI data center boom, memory chips, photonics, sensing hardware, and edge compute is the same foundation these robots will run on.
>
> Most people are watching the robot makers. Smart money is watching what goes inside every one of them.
>
> The Memory Supercycle No One’s Talking About Yet
>
> • Memory demand is about to get a powerful second leg that compounds through the 2030s
> • AI data centers are already strained on HBM and high-performance DRAM supply
> • Physical AI adds massive new volume from edge inference, sensor fusion, and real-time control at scale
> • One advanced humanoid can consume memory bandwidth and capacity comparable to several high-end AI servers today
>
> Why Robots Need So Much Memory
>
> • Real-time on-device AI inference (no latency for cloud round-trips in dynamic environments)
> • Heavy sensor fusion across cameras, LiDAR, tactile/force sensors, IMUs, and proprioception
> • Complex whole-body control, balance, dexterous hands, mapping, planning, and task memory
> • Training + simulation workloads in data centers also scale as robot fleets generate petabytes of real-world data
>
> Micron’s CEO said it plainly: humanoid robots carry roughly 10x the memory of an average L2+ autonomous vehicle, and he sees a sustained, substantial multi-decade memory demand cycle beginning in the latter part of this decade.
>
> The Stack Overlap Is Direct
> The photonics for high-speed interconnects, advanced packaging, and memory architectures built for AI accelerators transfer almost seamlessly to robotics. Training data centers and edge robots are two sides of the same infrastructure coin.
>
> Big Tech Is Already Building This Internally
>
> • Tesla → Optimus humanoid for internal factories + future external use
> • Amazon → Deep into warehouse robotics (Agility bots already deployed) and pushing further into AI-driven physical automation
>
> They may design custom systems in-house, but the advanced memory still comes from the specialists who can deliver at scale.
>
> Winners & Timeline
> • Micron ( $MU ), SK Hynix, and Samsung — the big three memory leaders
> • H2 2026 into 2027 is when multiple pure-play robotics companies are expected to go public (more visibility and capital)
> • Memory capacity build-out is happening now because these companies see combined AI infra + robotics demand as structural, not cyclical
>
> How to Get Exposure (You May Already Own It)
>
> One clean, targeted way: the Roundhill Memory ETF ( $DRAM ) is built specifically for pure memory exposure (HBM, DRAM, NAND) unlike broader semiconductor funds.
>
> Recent top holdings include: 
> • Samsung Electronics ~25.8% 
> • Micron (MU) ~25.45% 
> • SK hynix ~24.56%
> Together,  these three leaders make up over 75% of the ETF.
>
> Of course there are nuances to the timeline and risks:
>
> Nuance & Balanced View
> •Tech, cost, battery, safety, and regulatory hurdles remain real
> •Memory has historically been cyclical, but AI + Physical AI together are making demand more structural and multi-decade
> •Supply response is coming (new fabs from all three players), yet advanced memory shortages have already persisted, and new demand legs matter
> •Geopolitical concentration in the supply chain adds volatility but also reinforces the moat for leaders who execute
>
> The chart makes the signal impossible to ignore, the Q1 ’26 bar towers over everything before it. That capital is accelerating R&D, pilots, and supply chain prep right now.
>
> Physical AI is next.
>
> The memory supercycle already running from AI data centers just got a powerful second engine, and the same companies winning in AI silicon are best positioned for what comes next in the physical world.
>
> Not financial advice. This is one perspective on a long-term theme. 
> $MU $DRAM $AMZN $TSLA 000660.KS (SK hynix) | 005930.KS (Samsung)

### JASON CHAN (@phantom2008012)
_Sat Jun 27 17:39:35 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/phantom2008012/status/2070925020805931360)

> ちょうど昨日Zackの記事もありました、GFSとUMCの投資ロジックの違いについて
>
> 1. 成長ドライバー：シリコンフォトニクス vs. 22nm成熟プロセス
>  GlobalFoundries (GFS) —— 高成長なニッチ市場への注力：
> GFSはターゲットを絞ったアプローチをとっており、AIやデータセンターのインフラ需要を直接取り込んでいます。特に、光通信向けのシリコンフォトニクス (Silicon Photonics) 技術が牽引しており、2026年には同事業の売上が倍増、2028年末にはランレートで10億ドルを突破する見込みです。また、高周波通信向けのシリコンゲルマニウム (SiGe) ターンキーソリューションは2027年までキャパシティが埋まっています。AI光通信チェーンや欧米のローカルサプライチェーンのテーマに投資したい場合、GFSのストーリーは非常に魅力的です。
>  UMC (聯電) —— 規模の経済とコスト効率：
> UMCは成熟プロセスの雄であり、主力である22nmプラットフォームが業績を支えています。2026年末までに50社以上の顧客がテープアウト（設計完了）を予定しており、ディスプレイ駆動ICやマイクロコントローラ（MCU）など、幅広い汎用チップを網羅しています。GFSのような派手なAIインフラのテーマ性は薄いものの、Intelと共同開発している12nmプロセスが2027年に量産開始予定であり、将来的に高付加価値市場への参入ロードマップを描いています。
>
> 2. 財務パフォーマンスとバリュエーション
> 直近の2026年第1四半期（Q1）決算では、両社ともに売上総利益率（グロス・マージン）を約29%に維持していますが、その中身は異なります。
>  GFS（バリュエーションは高め、長期的価格支配力）： スマートフォン市場の減速によりモバイル部門が逆風を受けているものの、デザインウィン（設計獲得）が前年同期比で50%急増しています。これは顧客の囲い込みが順調である証拠であり、長期的な価格支配力の強さを示しています。
>  UMC（稼働率回復による短期的な利益爆発力）： Q1の設備稼働率が79%（前年同期から10ポイント上昇）まで回復したことで、営業レバレッジが効き、純利益が大幅に急増しました。また、UMCは伝統的に配当が安定しており配当利回りが高いため、インカムゲインを重視する投資家にとっても安心感があります。
>
> 3. どちらが今日の優れた投資機会か？
> 投資スタイルやポートフォリオの戦略によって結論が分かれます。
> 📥 GlobalFoundries (GFS) を選ぶべきケース：
> 長期的なアルファ（市場平均を超える超過リターン）を狙う場合です。
> 主力であるモバイル向けビジネスが2026年後半まで高一桁の減少を見込むなど短期的には逆風がありますが、米国・ドイツ・シンガポールに分散された製造拠点は、地政学的リスクを嫌う大手クライアント（Appleやルネサスなど）のニーズに合致しています。プレミアムなマルチプル（株価倍率）を許容し、AIインフラや光ネットワークへの構造転換に賭けたい投資家向けです。
> 📥 UMC (聯電) を選ぶべきケース：
> 景気サイクル好転による安心感と、確実なキャッシュフローを狙う場合です。
> 現在のUMCの主な懸念点は、シンガポール工場の拡張に伴う巨額の減価償却費であり、これが2026年後半の利益率を圧迫するリスクがあります。しかし、世界的な自動車、産業、家電向けチップの需要が本格的に回復すると予想する場合、稼働率上昇がそのまま利益に直結する高い財務レバレッジと、下値リスクを抑える高配当（防衛力）を兼ね備えた、バランスの良い循環株として非常に優秀です。

### ItsSmacky (@Chaamacoo)
_Sat Jun 27 17:54:24 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 311 · ↻ 43 · 💬 16 · [open on X](https://x.com/Chaamacoo/status/2070928748308807846)

> Reflections in the Dip: Why My Conviction in $SIVE Has Never Been Stronger
>
> I’ve been watching the recent pullback with a strange sense of calm.
>
> Weak hands are panicking. That’s what they do when the price moves against them for a few weeks. But if you’ve been here before, you know this feeling isn’t new, it’s just the market doing what it always does to test conviction.
>
> Over two years ago we were trading around 1.8 SEK. That drop felt brutal at the time. This one? This is noise compared to that. And yet the company is in a completely different place today.
>
> We’re still in an industry that hasn’t really started yet. Photonics for AI data centers is still pre-ramp for most people. There are no shiny consumer products on shelves for the average investor to point at and say “that’s what I own.” No flashy earnings beats every quarter. Just deep technology, long qualification cycles, and a market that very few truly understand. Most people want to see something they can touch before they believe. That’s why these moves feel so violent, because the narrative isn’t obvious until it suddenly is.
>
> That’s also why wireless has been so important. It’s been the quiet engine running in the background, delivering real revenue and building the foundation while photonics gets ready for its moment. Most of the market still doesn’t price that in properly. They’re too focused on the “when does photonics happen?” question and miss that the company is already executing on multiple fronts.
>
> I expect photonics news and orders from Ayar Labs, $POET, O-Net, $AEVA and $JBL before the year is out. Those won’t just be headlines, they’ll be real validation that starts to de-risk the story and reduce some of this volatility. I’m 100% convinced of that. Not because I’m hoping. Because I’ve followed this company long enough to know how it works.
>
> Nobody believes until it’s too late.
>
> We saw it from 4 SEK to over 100 SEK. Almost nobody saw that coming when it was actually happening. The next leg won’t be any different.
>
> There’s a lot of games being played right now, short sellers, institutions, traders all trying to take their piece. That’s normal when a stock has moved this much. It will stop when they’re done. Right now we’re also at a price level where a lot of serious money starts paying attention again. Don’t let the noise fool you.
>
> Do your own work.
>
> Read the presentations. Watch the CMDs. Look at the customer pipeline, the partnerships, the technology edge. Build your own picture instead of scrolling through what everyone else is saying.
>
> If you don’t believe light is the future of high-speed connectivity, that’s fine. There are plenty of other sectors. But if you do understand the technology and what Sivers actually brings to the table, the differentiated InP platform, the asset-light model, the real design wins, then the choice becomes pretty obvious.
>
> This is still a market that very few people truly grasp. A market that doesn’t even fully know how big it can get. And if you play it right, it rewards patience like few others.
> I actually believe more in $SIVEF today than I did a couple of years ago.
>
> Why? Because I can see the moves that are coming. Dual listing preparations are real. They’re not walking onto Nasdaq empty-handed. Watch what happens over the next few months. A lot of people are going to wish they had listened earlier.
>
> For what it’s worth, I haven’t sold a single share. And I won’t. The day I sell is the day the company stops delivering. Not when the stock has a bad week. Not when the noise gets loud. Price and company are two different things.
>
> This is still the early innings.
>
> Stay calm. Do the work. Trust what you know.

### AlchemistOracle (@AlchmstOraclee)
_Sat Jun 27 17:55:27 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 3 · ↻ 1 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/AlchmstOraclee/status/2070929013087080810)

> 🧵 My personal market heuristic after tracking AI infrastructure themes closely:
>
> Markets tend to price things in ~8 months in advance — except Space, Robotics, and Quantum, where sentiment runs well ahead of fundamentals.
>
> Here's how I'm applying it across themes I follow: 👇
>
> Photonics has a clear roadmap:
>
> • 1.6T pluggables ( $LITE, $COHR, $AAOI) are hitting now
> • CPO Scale-Out ramp: late H2 2026
> • CPO Scale-Up (Ayar, Celestial, etc.): H2 2027
>
> By the 8M rule, CPO Scale-Up names are still ~4 months early to position heavily.
>
> Memory is mid-bottleneck and re-rating accordingly:
>
> • HBM3e: now ($MU, Samsung, SK Hynix)
> • HBM4 mass production: ramping now
> • HBF: 2027
>
> Same players across cycles = compounding opportunity as each architecture matures.
>
> Glass Substrates:
>
> • SKC Absolics early ramp: H2 2026
> • Volume inflection: H2 2027–2028
> • TSMC CoPoS, Samsung, others: 2027–2028
>
> Machine/equipment suppliers here tend to see revenue before the volume ramp — worth noting for positioning.
>
> Neoclouds: Q4 2026 earnings looks like a key inflection window for leading players.
>
> In hindsight, March 2026 was the entry, not September 2025. The ~8M rule would've caught that.
>
> Current repositioning focus:
> • Memory
> • Neoclouds
> • Photonics
> • Robotics
>
> Preference for names capturing multiple themes simultaneously (e.g., pluggable + NPO + CPO exposure) and tactical exposure to bottleneck plays like advanced packaging and MLCCs.
>
> Key personal lesson: Avoid heavy exposure to names 12M+ out. Early conviction is fine — overweighting too early is where sizing discipline matters most.
>
> Still learning. These are just my own frameworks — not advice. 🙏

### AgAu Element (@AgAuElements)
_Sat Jun 27 17:55:44 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/AgAuElements/status/2070929086076346511)

> Retail is waiting for pure-play robotics IPOs, while institutional money is quietly locking up the raw physical supply chains today.
>
> The vertical spike highlighted confirms a massive paradigm shift: capital is moving aggressively into physical, embodied AI. As the first pure-play humanoid exits open the liquidity floodgates for H2 into 2027, the structural allocation war we are seeing in data centers will expand exponentially into robotics.
>
> The smart money is front-running this cross-exposure overlap through critical upstream hardware:
>  The Memory Squeeze Phase II: A humanoid robot running dense, real-time localized inference models requires up to a 10x memory multiplier over regular edge hardware. The exact same HBM, DRAM, and NAND components currently supply-constrained through 2027 to feed hyperscalers are facing an entirely new, massive downstream demand sink.
>  The Photonics Vision Choke Point: You cannot run autonomous, real-time spatial manipulation on a gutted hardware spec sheet. Next-gen FMCW LiDAR vision and sensor frameworks rely directly on high-power DFB laser chips. Companies like $AAOI or $LITE that control internal MOCVD crystal growth foundries aren't just building for transceivers—they are the literal gatekeepers of the physical optical sensing layer that every single humanoid platform requires to operate safely.
>
> The Upstream Component Leverage: Retail is waiting for pure-play robotics IPOs to buy the hype, completely missing that the absolute pricing power sits with the upstream component layer right now. Whether the end-program is run by $TSLA , $AMZN or a venture-backed pure-play, they all must secure raw, physical capacity from the exact same tightly contracted component suppliers.
>
> The cognition bottleneck has officially shifted to a physical execution bottleneck. When the factories are fully booked through mid-2027 just to satisfy data center demand, adding a multi-billion dollar humanoid hardware ramp into the equation means the choke points capture all the structural alpha.
>
> Accumulating the physical plumbing before the global IPO season reprices the entire supply chain. Long the bottlenecks. 📈🤖🧠

### Benniji (@BennyLam)
_Sat Jun 27 18:12:45 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/BennyLam/status/2070933367877505117)

> Nvidia quietly became the #1 data center Ethernet switch vendor — $2.1B revenue, 21.5% market share, up from 4% two years ago. IDC calls it 'one of the most significant vendor landscape shifts' in enterprise networking history. The networking business tripled to $15B.
>
> The obvious read: Nvidia is diversifying beyond GPUs.
>
> The more strategic read: Nvidia is identifying the next AI bottleneck before it fully materializes, then buying or building the solution before anyone else realizes it's a problem.
>
> At million-GPU cluster scale, the binding constraint isn't compute or even memory anymore. It's the fabric connecting them. Copper interconnects hit hard walls on power, bandwidth density, and reach. GPU utilization tanks when all-reduce and collective communication across racks can't keep up.
>
> Every cluster operator has experienced this: plenty of FLOPs, terrible effective throughput because the network is the bottleneck.
>
> Nvidia saw this coming when it bought Mellanox for $6.9B in 2019. Spectrum-X now generates more revenue than all Ethernet networking peers combined, per Jensen. The company is vertically integrating end-to-end cluster fabric the same way it integrated CUDA into the software stack.
>
> The next phase: photonics. Nvidia's CPO roadmap with TSMC COUPE is preparing for optical interconnects at the rack level. Bandwidth per AI rack goes from ~130 TB/s to multiples beyond that.
>
> Here's the under-covered part: the photonics supply chain — lasers, silicon photonics foundries, fiber attach, packaging — is even earlier in its high-volume ramp than HBM was in 2024. The qualification cycles are longer, yields lower, and the ecosystem less mature.
>
> The AI bottleneck narrative has shifted: compute → memory → networking → optics.
>
> $15B in networking revenue is the market signaling the next constraint. The companies that solve the photonics supply chain will be the Micron and SK Hynix of the next cycle.
>
> #Nvidia #Photonics #AIChips #Networking

### Paul LeCoque (@paullecoque)
_Sat Jun 27 20:25:30 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 46 · ↻ 3 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/paullecoque/status/2070966775655899482)

> $IONQ acquired Skyloom primarily for full-stack ownership and quantum-specific integration. 
>
> Quantum networking & entanglement focus: 
> Skyloom’s free-space optical tech (OCTs) provides the photonic layer for distributed quantum entanglement, quantum key distribution (QKD), and ultra-secure communications. 
>
> IonQ combines it with its quantum computing, ID Quantique (crypto), Vector Atomic (timing/sensing), and Capella (SAR satellites) assets to build an end-to-end quantum-secure space network. 
>
> Mynaric terminals (standard SDA-compatible laser links) excel at classical high-bandwidth data but lack native design for quantum state preservation or entanglement distribution.
>
> Vertical integration & control:
> Owning Skyloom gives IonQ full IP, customization, and supply-chain control for future satellites (transition announced for 2027+). Relying on Mynaric (now owned by competitor Rocket Lab) creates dependency risks. Skyloom was already SDA-qualified with strong delivery history (e.g., Tranche 1 terminals).
>
> Performance: 
> IonQ highlights potential boosts like up to 500% higher throughput and dramatically lower latency (hours → <1 hour) when paired with their ecosystem. Skyloom emphasizes secure, high-capacity LEO-LEO/LEO-ground links optimized for quantum-secure routing and defense applications.
>
> Skyloom vs. Mynaric: 
> •  Mynaric (CONDOR Mk3 etc.) — Proven, SDA-certified, used on Acadia-10 for 2.5 Gbps demos. Strong for classical SAR data relay and general OISL. Now scaled under Rocket Lab.
> •  Skyloom — Also SDA-certified/interoperable. Focuses on high-volume production, on-orbit routing, and integration with quantum/secure systems. Both meet similar SDA standards; differences are in optimization (e.g., Skyloom for quantum protocols, lower SWaP in some designs, or specific defense features).
>
> Bottom line: For a pure commercial SAR latency fix, Mynaric worked fine (as on Acadia-10). IonQ’s strategy is building a quantum internet / secure space backbone, where owning a tailored optical layer (Skyloom) + quantum hardware gives a differentiated, controllable platform.

### InterMariusz🇵🇱 (@TheUnmasker_PL)
_Sat Jun 27 20:39:05 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/TheUnmasker_PL/status/2070970192017183186)

> Dokładnie tak — z dobrym autopilotem (ArduPilot/iNav), solidnym montażem i dobrze skalibrowanym systemem da się wyciągnąć zaskakująco dużo nawet z przeciętnych sensorów MEMS. Wibracje, czas lotu i prędkość rzeczywiście mocno wpływają na dryf.Ale tu właśnie jest różnica.ANELLO X3 nie jest ulepszonym MEMS-em. To optyczny żyroskop (technologia SiPhOG – silicon photonics), który działa na zasadzie efektu Sagnaca, a nie wibrującej mechanicznej struktury.  Dzięki temu ma znacznie lepszą stabilność biasu (< 0,5°/h) i jest dużo mniej podatny na wibracje, temperaturę i przyspieszenia niż nawet dobre taktyczne MEMS-y.  To właśnie dlatego Amerykanie (i sektor obronny) w to wchodzą — bo chcą mieć wysoką precyzję inercji w małym, tanim i masowo produkowanym urządzeniu, a nie tylko „dobre wyniki przy idealnych warunkach i krótkim locie”.Z X3 dryf rośnie znacznie wolniej, więc przy dłuższym locie bez GPS (albo po utracie obrazu) różnica robi się już bardzo wyraźna — szczególnie przy RTH, w rojach czy przy misjach na 10–20+ km.Czyli nie chodzi o to, że „wcześniej było tragicznie”. Chodzi o to, że teraz da się to zrobić znacznie lepiej i taniej niż klasycznymi wojskowymi FOG-ami. Inaczej jaki sens byłby w ogóle w to wchodzić...

### John Galt (@AtlasShrug1)
_Sat Jun 27 21:17:43 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/AtlasShrug1/status/2070979915604996250)

> The $QQQ as launched in March of 1999.  The ETFs always arrive at exactly the wrong time, enabling the masses to plow into the most bloated, overvalued themes with ease and at little cost.  
>
> How does this look for AI?  You were early in mid 2023 and 2024.  Then in 2025 you were in the middle innings.  And now you are late anon, with many launches per month popping up in AI and related themes.  
>
> Everyone is in, and everyone is an expert. 
>
> Dozens of AI-related ETFs have launched in the past 3 years (roughly mid-2023 to mid-2026), contributing to a total of over 90 AI-themed ETFs now available in the US. 
> Key Context on Launches
> •  Pre-2023 baseline: A smaller number existed (e.g., broader robotics/AI funds like BOTZ or AIQ from earlier years). The post-ChatGPT AI boom (late 2022 onward) triggered a sharp increase in new, targeted launches. 
> •  Notable recent examples:
> •  2023: Roundhill Generative AI & Technology ETF (CHAT, launched May 2023) — one of the first pure generative AI-focused funds. 
> •  2024–2026: A wave including iShares A.I. Innovation and Tech Active ETF (BAI, Oct 2024), various Global X, Invesco, WisdomTree, First Trust, and niche products (e.g., memory/semiconductor photonics, pure-play AI infrastructure like DRAM in 2026). Multiple launches per month in peak periods, often active or thematic.

### John Galt (@AtlasShrug1)
_Sat Jun 27 21:22:24 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 4 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/AtlasShrug1/status/2070981094699147295)

> The notion of not being in photonics names bc they have already yielded the abnormally high returns doesnt really occur to you I guess.  Once this ends, these names won’t reemerge as new leadership.  They never do.  The new leadership will be in other sectors, and if you want to make money you’ll have to pivot.

### The Trend Sage (@JonkooTrades)
_Sat Jun 27 21:38:56 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 37 · ↻ 1 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/JonkooTrades/status/2070985256904057200)

> $SIVE is down here not because of anything Sivers did. 
>
> The entire photonics complex is in a drawdown, and that's exactly the kind of dislocation worth leaning into.
>
> What actually happened:
> On June 9, @SemiAnalysis_ published an institutional-only note flagging potential delays in CPO deployment, with a yield-based bear argument (their math: 95% per-engine yield compounded across 32 optical engines = ~19% system yield). 
>
> The note hit institutional desks first. The whole optical group sold off together: $AAOI -14%, $COHR -11%, $POET -12%, $LITE -8%, $MRVL -7.6%, and $SIVE -8.7% alongside them.
>
> Here's the tell. Under the exact same negative news, $AAOI fell ~17% intraday while Lumentum, with a highly overlapping technology profile, fell ~8%. Roughly a 2x difference in decline for two names exposed to the identical headline. 
>
> That spread is the signature of a positioning-driven shakeout flushing out the loosest hands (high retail concentration, high margin balances), not a calm fundamental repricing. 
>
> The names that bled most were the ones with the loosest float, not the ones with the worst fundamentals.
>
> This hit a sector that was up triple digits YTD. $AAOI +390%, $MRVL +228%, $LITE +138%, $COHR +107%, $POET +100%. $SOXX dropped while the $VIX barely moved. That combination, sharp single-name drawdowns with no systemic panic, is profit-taking and sector rotation off parabolic runs, not a demand collapse.
>
> And on the other side of the same week: $NVDA's own blog states Spectrum-X Ethernet Photonics is now in full production, with CPO-based next-gen Spectrum-X switching going into scale-out and scale-across deployments on the Vera Rubin platform. 
>
> The demand signal didn't break. A timing-and-magnitude call on the ramp got mistranslated by the time it reached retail into "CPO is cancelled," which it isn't.
>
> A CPO timing delay does not threaten the Sivers thesis the way it threatens a name priced for imminent volume.
>
> Sivers isn't trading on 2026 CPO revenue. The CPO ramp was always a 2027 qualification, 2028 volume story. 
>
> Even @aleabitoreddit, asked directly if the selloff shook it's faith in photonics, said they're more bullish as prices drop.
>
> When a quality supply-chain position gets sold purely because it shares a sector ETF with the names institutions are trimming, that's the dislocation you want. 
>
> Buying the bottleneck while the complex flushes weak hands is a better entry than chasing it green. 
>
> Just size it as the high-beta position it is, because the volatility that created this entry cuts both ways.
>
> If you are still bullish on $SIVE - drop a like!
>
> Not Financial Advice. DYOR.

---

### 바카닉올인 (@YooJoungilpe)
_Sat Jun 27 21:45:37 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 32 · ↻ 4 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/YooJoungilpe/status/2070986936899289424)

> $SIVE   AI분석
>
> 1. $SIVE (Sivers Semiconductors) 핵심 사업과 최근 뉴스
> Sivers Semiconductors는 스웨덴 회사로, 크게 두 축을 가지고 있습니다:
> •  Photonics 부문: InP 기반 고출력·협대역 CW DFB 레이저와 레이저 어레이. AI 데이터센터 광연결(CPO), FMCW LiDAR에 특화.
> •  Wireless 부문: mmWave 빔포머 IC (5G, Satcom, defense).
> 2026년 3월 발표된 LiDAR 뉴스가 정확히 사용자가 말한 내용입니다:
> •  전략적 LiDAR 고객이 자사 기술을 플랫폼 전체에 채택.
> •  2026년 Q4부터 생산 ramp 시작 (자동차 + 산업/로보틱스용).
> •  공급 품목: CW DFB 레이저 + 광증폭기.
> •  누적 수익 잠재력 $53M ~ $138M (고객 제품 수명 주기 기준).
> 이 고객은 공식 확인은 안 됐지만, 시장에서 Aeva로 강력하게 추정되고 있습니다. 이유:
> •  Aeva는 FMCW LiDAR 전문 (협대역·고출력 레이저가 핵심).
> •  Aeva + LG Innotek 전략 파트너십 (2025년 7월 발표, LG Innotek이 Aeva 모듈 제조·공급).
> •  Aeva는 로보틱스·휴머노이드·산업 자동화도 타겟팅하고 있음 (Boston Dynamics Atlas 같은 고급 비전 시스템에 잘 맞는 기술).
> 이게 바로 사용자가 말한 “$AEVA와 LG Innotek을 통해 공급망으로 들어온다”는 부분입니다. 2026년 말 생산 확대 + 상당한 수익 잠재력도 정확히 맞아요.
> 2. $SPCX (SpaceX 프록시) Mesh Optical 인수와의 연결고리
> 최근 뉴스 (2026년 6월 26일경): Musk/SpaceX 측이 Mesh Optical Technologies 인수에 FTC 승인 받음. Mesh는 전 SpaceX 엔지니어들이 만든 스타트업으로, AI 데이터센터용 1.6Tbps 광 트랜시버를 개발 중입니다. DFB 레이저를 사용하고, flip-chip 패키징 등 고효율 광 인터커넥트 기술.
> 연결 포인트:
> •  Mesh가 필요로 하는 핵심 부품 중 하나가 고성능 DFB 레이저 → Sivers가 정확히 만드는 제품.
> •  Sivers는 이미 Ayar Labs, POET Technologies 등 CPO(코패키지드 옵틱스) 플레이어에 공급 중.
> •  SpaceX/Starlink 생태계(레이저 기반 위성 간 통신) + xAI/Tesla 데이터센터 수요 증가 → 광·포토닉스 전반 수요 확대.
> •  X(트위터)에서도 최근 “Mesh 인수 후 SIVE가 레이저 공급으로 수혜”라는 언급이 나오고 있어요.
> 결론: LiDAR 뉴스 자체가 Mesh 인수와 “직접” 연결되는 건 아니지만, 전체 포토닉스/AI 인프라/Satcom 테마에서 시너지 효과가 분명히 있습니다. $SIVE가 “포토닉스 + LiDAR + Satcom” 3박자 비대칭 플레이인 건 맞아요.
> 3. 주가 상황과 투자 포인트
> •  52주 범위: 2.85 SEK ~ 110 SEK (고점 6월 2일).
> •  현재 (6월 26~27일경): 약 63 SEK 수준 → 고점 대비 약 42~43% 하락.
> •  YTD +1,400% 이상, 1년 +1,500% 이상 폭등 후 조정. “2000% 올랐으니 기다리자” 하던 사람들 입장에서는 정확히 조정 구간.
> 강점 (Bull case):
> •  AI 데이터센터 광연결(CPO) + 로보틱스 LiDAR + Satcom 수요가 동시에 터질 수 있는 희귀한 포지션.
> •  Opportunity pipeline 이미 $799M (2025년 말 대비 +77%).
> •  기술적으로 InP DFB 레이저에서 경쟁력 있음 (특히 narrow linewidth + high power).
> 리스크 (Bear case, 상당히 큼):
> •  극단적 고평가: trailing P/S 60x 이상. 많은 분석가들이 “과대평가”라고 지적.
> •  아직 적자 지속 (Q1 2026 revenue SEK 61.9M, 전년比 -22%, 손실 확대). 실행 리스크 높음.
> •  고객 집중 리스크, ramp 지연 가능성.
> •  과거 희석 이력 있음. 소형주(시총 약 18~19B SEK)라 변동성 극심.
> •  경쟁사: Coherent, Lumentum 등 대형 플레이어 존재.
> 종합 의견
> $SIVE에 극도로 bullish할 만한 근거는 충분합니다. 특히:
> •  Aeva/LG Innotek 공급망 + 2026년 Q4 ramp
> •  Mesh Optical 인수로 인한 포토닉스 테마 강화
> •  AI + 로보틱스 + Satcom 3중 수혜 가능성
> 고점 대비 40% 조정한 지금이 “겁먹고 포기할 타이밍”은 아니에요. 다만 고위험 speculative 종목이라는 점을 명확히 해야 합니다. valuation이 이미 많은 성공을 선반영하고 있어서, ramp가 늦어지거나 기대가 어긋나면 추가 조정도 충분히 나올 수 있어요.
> 지금 사야 할까?
> → 장기적으로 photonics/AI 인프라를 강하게 믿고, 변동성을 감당할 수 있다면 분할 매수 관점에서 관심 가질 만한 구간입니다.
> → 단기 트레이딩이나 “무조건 오른다” 마인드라면 리스크가 매우 큽니다.

### Gunnar Forsgren (@Gunnar_Forsgren)
_Sat Jun 27 23:33:31 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/Gunnar_Forsgren/status/2071014092630884485)

> Putin held a speech during their meeting:
>
> "I am pleased to welcome the participants and organizers of the 13th Forum of Regions of Russia and Belarus, which traditionally takes place on the eve of Independence Day of the Republic of Belarus, celebrated on July 3 and marking the anniversary of Minsk's liberation from the Nazi invaders.
>
> I sincerely congratulate all Belarusian friends on this national holiday. Russia will always remember that during the Great Patriotic War, our peoples, shoulder to shoulder and at enormous sacrifice, defended freedom and independence, bringing peace to Europe and all of humanity.
>
> It is important that Russia and Belarus carefully preserve and enhance their fraternal traditions of friendship and mutual assistance, strengthening their historically established cultural and spiritual ties. Russian-Belarusian relations are truly strategic, and our Union State serves as a model of mutually beneficial and equal integration, effectively facilitating the deepening of cooperation within such associations as the Eurasian Economic Union, the Commonwealth of Independent States, and the Collective Security Treaty Organization.
>
> One of the main driving forces behind the partnership between Russia and Belarus, as well as the construction of the Union State, are ties between regions. This is the solid foundation upon which cooperation between the two countries is steadily developing across a wide range of areas—political and security, social and humanitarian, and, of course, economic.
>
> Forums of Regions regularly bring together representatives of federal and local authorities, legislators and businesspeople, experts, and public figures—in short, all those who help establish and develop direct contacts between Russian and Belarusian regions.
>
> This year, more than 600 delegates from 73 constituent entities of the Russian Federation arrived in the capital of Belarus. Among them are governors, heads of regional legislative assemblies, deputies, ministers, and company executives. The Belarusian delegation is no less prestigious.
>
> The substantial package of agreements and commercial contracts signed during the forum demonstrates our mutual focus on achieving concrete results.
>
> You are discussing a truly relevant topic: "Economic Interaction between Regions – the Foundation for Sustainable Development of Russia and Belarus." I note that, thanks in large part to close interregional economic cooperation, bilateral trade turnover last year broke another record – $52 billion, according to our statistics. This year, growth continues – more than 7 percent in the first quarter. All mutual settlements between our countries are conducted in national currencies.
>
> The harmonization of legislation in trade, investment, and financial regulation is actively underway. Approaches in customs and tax matters are being unified, and a unified quality control system for goods is being implemented. The Union State Committee on Standardization and Quality held its first meeting during the forum.
>
> Russia leads the way in accumulated investment in the Belarusian economy, at approximately $4 billion. Companies with Russian capital operate in all regions of the republic, with approximately 2,500 of them nationwide.
>
> The regions are closely involved in the implementation of 26 joint import substitution projects in high-tech sectors. For example, modern mining equipment is being manufactured with Belarusian partners in the Moscow Region, machine tool components are being produced in the Novosibirsk Region, and equipment from the Minsk Tractor Plant is being assembled in Tatarstan.
>
> Production cooperation has been established between Belarusian civil aviation plants and the interregional cluster of the Irkutsk, Ulyanovsk, Nizhny Novgorod, and Voronezh Regions, which produces the MS-21 and Sukhoi Superjet 100 airliners. Design bureaus in the Sverdlovsk and Brest Regions are working on the Osvey light multirole aircraft project.
>
> Leading Belarusian factories Integral and Planar supply components for electronics manufacturing in Tatarstan and the Nizhny Novgorod and Moscow regions. Companies in Moscow, St. Petersburg, and Minsk have established effective cooperation chains for the production of optical devices and photonics instruments for communications, data transmission, and IT systems.
>
> Regular passenger flights operate from 10 Russian regions to Belarus. Cross-border commuter trains between Smolensk and Vitebsk and between Smolensk and Orsha were launched in April. Service between Velikiye Luki and Vitebsk, Velikiye Luki and Polotsk, and Bryansk and Gomel are next in line. Plans include the construction of a high-speed railway between Moscow and Minsk.
>
> The railway and port infrastructure of Russian regions is being used to transport Belarusian exports. A permit-free transit procedure is being gradually introduced for Russian and Belarusian goods transported to third countries by road."

### Gunnar Forsgren (@Gunnar_Forsgren)
_Sat Jun 27 23:41:38 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/Gunnar_Forsgren/status/2071016134057361748)

> Here is what Putin spoke:
> "I am pleased to welcome the participants and organizers of the 13th Forum of Regions of Russia and Belarus, which traditionally takes place on the eve of Independence Day of the Republic of Belarus, celebrated on July 3 and marking the anniversary of Minsk's liberation from the Nazi invaders.
>

Russian-Belarusian relations are truly strategic, and our Union State serves as a model of mutually beneficial and equal integration, effectively facilitating the deepening of cooperation within such associations as the Eurasian Economic Union, the Commonwealth of Independent States, and the Collective Security Treaty Organization.
>

This is the solid foundation upon which cooperation between the two countries is steadily developing across a wide range of areas—political and security, social and humanitarian, and, of course, economic.
>
> Forums of Regions regularly bring together representatives of federal and local authorities, legislators and businesspeople, experts, and public figures—in short, all those who help establish and develop direct contacts between Russian and Belarusian regions.
>
> This year, more than 600 delegates from 73 constituent entities of the Russian Federation arrived in the capital of Belarus. Among them are governors, heads of regional legislative assemblies, deputies, ministers, and company executives. The Belarusian delegation is no less prestigious.
>
> The substantial package of agreements and commercial contracts signed during the forum demonstrates our mutual focus on achieving concrete results.
>
> You are discussing a truly relevant topic: "Economic Interaction between Regions – the Foundation for Sustainable Development of Russia and Belarus." I note that, thanks in large part to close interregional economic cooperation, bilateral trade turnover last year broke another record – $52 billion, according to our statistics. This year, growth continues – more than 7 percent in the first quarter. All mutual settlements between our countries are conducted in national currencies.
>
> The harmonization of legislation in trade, investment, and financial regulation is actively underway. Approaches in customs and tax matters are being unified, and a unified quality control system for goods is being implemented. The Union State Committee on Standardization and Quality held its first meeting during the forum.
>
> Russia leads the way in accumulated investment in the Belarusian economy, at approximately $4 billion. Companies with Russian capital operate in all regions of the republic, with approximately 2,500 of them nationwide.
>
> The regions are closely involved in the implementation of 26 joint import substitution projects in high-tech sectors. For example, modern mining equipment is being manufactured with Belarusian partners in the Moscow Region, machine tool components are being produced in the Novosibirsk Region, and equipment from the Minsk Tractor Plant is being assembled in Tatarstan.
>
> Production cooperation has been established between Belarusian civil aviation plants and the interregional cluster of the Irkutsk, Ulyanovsk, Nizhny Novgorod, and Voronezh Regions, which produces the MS-21 and Sukhoi Superjet 100 airliners. Design bureaus in the Sverdlovsk and Brest Regions are working on the Osvey light multirole aircraft project.
>
> Leading Belarusian factories Integral and Planar supply components for electronics manufacturing in Tatarstan and the Nizhny Novgorod and Moscow regions. Companies in Moscow, St. Petersburg, and Minsk have established effective cooperation chains for the production of optical devices and photonics instruments for communications, data transmission, and IT systems."
>
> Regular passenger flights operate from 10 Russian regions to Belarus. Cross-border commuter trains between Smolensk and Vitebsk and between Smolensk and Orsha were launched in April. Service between Velikiye Luki and Vitebsk, Velikiye Luki and Polotsk, and Bryansk and Gomel are next in line. Plans include the construction of a high-speed railway between Moscow and Minsk.
>
> The railway and port infrastructure of Russian regions is being used to transport Belarusian exports. A permit-free transit procedure is being gradually introduced for Russian and Belarusian goods transported to third countries by road.
