> Dear @vonderleyen,
> How wonderful that you and the entire College of Commissioners travelled to Cork today to visit the Tyndall National Institute! A real “innovation powerhouse,” as you so aptly put it. “From test to scale, from ideas to industry” – that sounds like proper European future music. And Ireland really is a beautiful country. The green hills, the Guinness, the friendly people… a business trip like that must be quite enjoyable. The European taxpayer is surely delighted that you’re all so motivated and on the road.
> Just one small, modest question out of pure fiscal curiosity: Did you know that right on your doorstep in Leuven, Belgium, there is an institute that is considered the global benchmark in exactly this field – integrated semiconductors, nanoelectronics, photonics and deep-tech hardware?
> imec employs over 6,500 scientists, engineers and innovators from more than 100 countries. That’s more than ten times the size of Tyndall (which had a proud 580 staff and students in 2024, including 173 postgraduates with 158 PhD students). imec was Belgium’s top patent applicant in 2024/2025 and is driving major European Chips Act pilot lines. While Tyndall is getting an expansion worth over €100 million and works with around 200 industry partners, imec has had a global network for years and generates well over a billion euros in revenue annually – mostly through direct industry collaborations.
> But of course: why stay in Leuven when you can fly the whole College, security teams, protocol staff and all the rest to Ireland instead? The taxpayers in Germany, France, Italy and all the other member states are happy to pay for a bit of extra European unity – plus flights, hotels, escorted convoys and the entire logistical effort for a visit to Cork, when Leuven is only about a half-hour drive from Brussels.
> We really do think it’s nice that you praise Tyndall so much. The institute has been doing good work since it was founded in 2004 (with roots in the NMRC from 1981). But if you’re going to celebrate European top-tier research, then please do it where it’s biggest, most established and closest. It would save money – and CO₂. The Irish government can still be happy anyway – they’ve already received plenty of EU funds.
> With friendly but slightly puzzled regards,

### Sensei (@Sensei0701)
_Thu Jul 02 19:53:54 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 7 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/Sensei0701/status/2072770760519925941)

> $COHR $LITE $AAOI 
>
> The recent hammering of photonics/CPO names, which was partly triggered by the SemiAnalysis note pushing timelines out for CPO adoption, looks like a short-sighted overreaction rather than a collapse in the fundamental thesis imo.
>
> The realistic path is to use copper for scale-up as long as you can on short-reach, low-latency links inside the rack/cluster, and then move to optics as the final phase of the transition. The move to optics is fundamentally necessary. Copper interconnects eventually hit physical limits w/ exponentially rising power draw, signal degradation, and restricted reach as AI clusters scale to massive sizes w/ extreme bandwidth demands. Copper simply cannot efficiently move data across longer distances and at the densities required w/o consuming unsustainable power or compromising performance. 
>
> This hybrid, phased reality is not a bear case. Copper staying relevant longer actually extends the runway and de-risks CPO adoption as clusters scale to a point where copper hits hard walls.
>
> We’re still early in the multi-year AI infrastructure buildout. The “slow ramp” narrative today is exactly what you should be expect anyways before the volumes compound in the back half of the decade.

### Y. Putterman (@pwtrmn74007)
_Thu Jul 02 21:14:01 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/pwtrmn74007/status/2072790924996886633)

> The Market That Changed Engines Mid‑Flight Strategic & Tactical Read of the Day 
>
> Today's tape told a story that wasn't subtle: the market didn't break, it pivoted. Momentum the great engine of the 2025–H1 2026 rally finally lost altitude. Semiconductors, memory, photonics, and the AI‑power complex all slipped into a decisive unwind. META admitted AI progress has been slower than expected; photonics rejected their 21‑DMA; semis logged a second straight 5%+ selloff; MTUM printed its sixth rare >3% down day while RSP rose. That's not noise that's regime change.
>
> Yet beneath the surface, the bull market kept breathing. Defensive sectors surged: healthcare, staples, utilities, materials. Equal‑weight advanced. The Dow hit a record. Investors didn't de‑risk they reallocated. This is classic bull‑market rotation: money staying in equities, but choosing different leaders.
>
> Macro reinforced the shift. Payrolls softened, real earnings remain pressured, and factory orders ex‑transport were solid a mix that tempers rate‑hike fears without signaling recession. Micro confirmed it: hyperscalers stabilizing, domestic cyclicals strengthening, and median earnings tracking double‑digit growth. The bottleneck trade is crowded; the broader market is not.
>
> Strategically, leadership is migrating from AI‑momentum to diversified, cash‑flow‑rich, domestically leveraged sectors. Tactically, expect digestion in semis and selective strength in defensives until Q2 earnings clarify whether AI re‑accelerates or hands the baton to the rest of the market.
>
> Bull markets don't die when leaders tire they evolve when new ones emerge.
>
> And to all American readers: Happy Independence Day may your portfolios enjoy some fireworks too. 🇺🇸✨

### Crypto Quantum｜量子株・IonQ (@CryptoQuantumjp)
_Thu Jul 02 21:33:25 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/CryptoQuantumjp/status/2072795806101635085)

> 【研究開発】
> 米NSFが量子フォトニクス実用化へ400万ドル追加支援。GPS不要の量子ナビゲーションを視野に、最終段階では最大5,500万ドル規模の量子センター構想へ発展する可能性。
> （2026年7月3日 〔日本時間〕・The Quantum Insider）
>
> 何が起きたか：
> 米ミシガン大学が主導する量子フォトニクス研究プロジェクト「QuPID（Quantum Photonic Integration and Deployment）」が、米国立科学財団（NSF）のNational Quantum Virtual Laboratory（NQVL）プログラムのフェーズ2に採択され、2年間で400万ドル（約6億円、1ドル=150円換算）の助成を受けることになった。これはフェーズ1の100万ドル（約1.5億円）に続く資金で、将来的には最大5,500万ドル（約82.5億円）のNSF量子センターへ発展する可能性がある。研究では、量子状態の光を利用した集積フォトニクスチップを開発し、GPSが使えない水中・宇宙・月面などでも利用できる高精度ナビゲーションや超高精度センシングを目指す。プロジェクトにはオハイオ州立大学、ハーバード大学、スタンフォード大学、パデュー大学のほか、Honeywell、TOPTICA Photonics、General Motors、Toyota、Raytheon、NASA Glenn Research Center、Air Force Research Laboratoryなど産学官が参加している。 
>
> 読み解き：
> このニュースの本質は、「量子コンピュータ」ではなく「量子フォトニクス」の商用化に研究資金の重心が移っている点にある。今回の目標は演算性能ではなく、量子光学を使った実環境向けセンサーやナビゲーションであり、量子技術をインフラへ組み込む流れを象徴している。
>
> 特にNSFがフェーズ制で資金を拡大し、最終的には数千万ドル規模の量子センターを構想していることは、単なる大学研究ではなく、量産・実装を前提としたエコシステム形成を狙っていることを示す。さらに、自動車メーカー、防衛企業、NASAまで参加していることから、出口市場が明確な研究テーマとして位置付けられている点も重要だ。
>
> 量子業界では計算機だけでなく、量子センシングや量子通信が商用化を先行する可能性が高いと見られており、今回の支援はその流れを裏付ける動きといえる。 
>
> 評価：
> ・業界インパクト：★★★
> ・注目度：★★★
> ・関連銘柄：HON, GM, TM
>
> 結論：
> 量子技術の競争軸は計算能力だけではなく、センシングやナビゲーションなど現実世界の用途へ広がりつつある。今後は、このような研究プロジェクトが実証実験や政府調達へ発展するかどうかが、商用化を見極める重要なポイントになる。
>
> 出典：The Quantum Insider
> （https://t.co/QtN8toTdiS）

---

### Crypto Quantum｜量子株・IonQ (@CryptoQuantumjp)
_Thu Jul 02 21:34:25 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/CryptoQuantumjp/status/2072796057298424181)

> 【量子ハードウェア】
> Pasqalがカナダで光集積回路（PIC）実装拠点を新設。790万ドル（約11.9億円、1ドル=150円換算）規模で量子・センシング向け製造基盤を強化。
> （2026年7月3日 日本時間、Quantum Computing Report）
>
> 何が起きたか：
> Pasqalは、買収したカナダ子会社Aeponyxを通じて、ケベック州ブロモンのC2MI（MiQro Innovation Collaborative Center）内に、光集積回路（PIC）パッケージングの専門拠点を設立すると発表した。 
>
> このプロジェクトは総額790万ドル（約11.9億円、1ドル=150円換算）で、うち400万ドル（約6.0億円）は連邦・州政府が支援し、その中にはNGen（Next Generation Manufacturing Canada）からの300万ドル（約4.5億円）が含まれる。 
>
> 拠点では、シリコンナイトライド（SiN）フォトニクスを活用したPICの実装・組立ラインを構築し、レーザー制御モジュールなど量子コンピュータや量子センシングに必要な光部品の量産体制を整える。初期は試作・少量生産を担い、将来的には年間50万個超のモジュール生産能力を目指す計画だ。HOP Technologies、Phantom Photonicsも参画し、医療センシングやLiDARなど量子以外の用途も視野に入れる。 
>
> 読み解き：
> 今回のポイントは「量子コンピュータを作る」ことではなく、「量子コンピュータを量産できる部品産業を作る」ことにある。
>
> 量子コンピュータではチップそのもの以上に、レーザー、光導波路、ファイバー接続などの光学実装が製造ボトルネックになりやすい。特に中性原子方式は多数のレーザーを高精度で制御する必要があり、PICの高品質な実装技術は性能だけでなく生産性にも直結する。 
>
> 興味深いのは、この拠点が量子専用工場ではなく、防衛向けLiDARや医療センシング企業も巻き込んだ共通インフラとして設計されている点だ。同じフォトニクス製造設備を複数産業で共有できれば、量子産業単独では難しい設備投資の採算性を高められる。近年は各国が「量子主権」を意識したサプライチェーン整備を進めているが、この発表も製造能力そのものを国内に確保する流れの一例と言える。Pasqalにとっても、Aeponyx買収後の垂直統合を具体的な製造基盤へ発展させる動きとして位置付けられる。 
>
> 評価：
> ・業界インパクト：★★★
> ・注目度：★★★
> ・関連銘柄：PASQAL（未上場）
>
> 結論：
> 量子業界ではプロセッサ性能だけでなく、「安定して作れる製造基盤」が競争力になり始めている。今後は各社が光部品やパッケージング、製造拠点への投資をどこまで拡大するかが、商用展開の速度を左右する重要な指標になりそうだ。
>
> 出典：Quantum Computing Report
> (https://t.co/kVpXEuzfHj)

### Jason's Chips (@jasonschips)

> 🔔 The Daily Semi-Cap — July 2, 2026
>
> 📊 SMH: $592.29 (-4.54%)
>
> 📈 Earnings:
> • No new semiconductor earnings released today.
>
> 🔥 Major Developments:
> • AXT-Tongmei signed a three-year 6-inch InP wafer substrate capacity agreement with Coherent, including a $22.3M prepayment tied to expanded Beijing capacity from 2026-2028. The optics supply chain is moving from spot-market scramble to locked capacity, which matters for Coherent, AXT, and the broader AI photonics bottleneck.
> • Anthropic is exploring a custom AI chip with Samsung as a potential manufacturing partner, evaluating Samsung’s 2nm process and advanced packaging. If it moves forward, the read-through is bigger than one AI lab: frontier model companies are trying to control silicon roadmaps, and Samsung is still hunting for a marquee AI foundry win against TSMC.
> • Nvidia is offering smaller GPU cloud providers financial backstops and revenue-share structures tied to unused GPU capacity. That supports near-term accelerator demand, but it also makes the AI infrastructure stack more circular: chip demand, cloud financing, and end-customer utilization are becoming increasingly intertwined.
> • Meta said AI agent development over the last four months has not accelerated as expected, adding pressure to the capex ROI debate after reports that it may sell excess AI compute capacity. The takeaway is not that AI demand is dead; it is that hyperscaler capex now needs cleaner monetization proof, not just bigger buildout numbers.

### TheValueist (@TheValueist)
_Thu Jul 02 22:02:29 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 66 · ↻ 5 · 💬 6 · [open on X](https://x.com/TheValueist/status/2072803120984297485)

> $AXTI $COHR Do you believe this is last InP prepayment deal that will be cut over the next 5 years? We merely getting started.
> ———————-
> BOTTOM LINE: This is incrementally bullish for COHR fundamentals but more strategically important than financially material. It confirms that 6-inch InP substrate supply remains a gating item for COHR’s AI optical ramp, validates AXT/Tongmei as a meaningful 6-inch InP substrate supplier, and shows COHR is using customer-style capacity prepayments upstream to lock supply through the next 3 years. It should be more stock-moving for AXTI than COHR, but for COHR it is a positive de-risking datapoint after a weak tape day, not a thesis-changing event by itself.
>
> The agreement is straightforward but important. AXT-Tongmei entered a 3-year Master Development and Supply Agreement with Coherent, effective June 25, 2026, covering “mass development and supply” of 6-inch indium phosphide wafer substrates. AXT will expand capacity at its Beijing facility from 2026 through 2028, Coherent will make a $22.2885M prepayment for committed capacity, wafer prices are pre-established, and the prepayment will be applied against future product purchases. Coherent also gets refund rights if unused amounts remain at expiry or termination, and can terminate and recover unused prepayment if AXT fails to meet the capacity commitment for more than 6 successive months. AXT gets protection if Coherent misses minimum order quantities, in which case unused prepayment becomes nonrefundable and AXT can terminate. AXT must also offer additional capacity beyond the committed quantity to Coherent on the same terms. The full agreement will not be available until AXT files its Q2 2026 10-Q.  
>
> The key interpretation is that this is not about outsourcing COHR’s differentiated InP device manufacturing. AXT is supplying 6-inch InP wafer substrates, the upstream crystalline substrate input. Coherent still does the value-added photonic device work: EMLs, CW lasers, photodiodes, PICs and related integration. That distinction matters because COHR’s moat remains process/yield/device manufacturing and vertical integration; AXT is enabling more wafer starts, not replacing COHR’s 6-inch InP fab advantage.
>
> For COHR, the positive read is supply-chain de-risking. Management has repeatedly framed InP capacity as the key constraint in the AI optical cycle, while also saying 6-inch InP is central to the revenue and gross margin ramp. In the May earnings call, COHR said its 6-inch platform was producing EMLs, CW lasers and photodiodes, with yields exceeding 3-inch lines, first 6-inch-derived transceiver shipments already contributing to revenue and margin, and internal InP capacity expected to double ahead of plan and more than double again by the end of calendar 2027.   This AXT agreement strengthens confidence that substrate availability will not become the hidden bottleneck that prevents those internal wafer starts from scaling.
>
> This also lines up with the J.P. Morgan investor-meeting takeaway that COHR had substrate supply “locked in” across 5 suppliers spanning multiple geographies, several capable of producing 6-inch substrates. The AXT filing effectively names 1 of those upstream supply arrangements and shows there is real money, fixed pricing, and committed capacity behind the company’s prior substrate comments.  
>
> The less bullish read is that the deal confirms the bottleneck is real and persistent. Coherent would not be making take-or-pay-like commitments and prepaying a supplier for 3-year capacity if 6-inch InP substrates were abundant. Reuters recently reported that China’s InP export controls have disrupted the AI photonics supply chain, that AXT and Sumitomo dominate global InP substrate production, that AXT is a major supplier to Coherent, and that 6-inch InP wafer prices have reportedly risen sharply since China tightened export licensing.   The agreement helps COHR, but it does not eliminate geopolitical risk because the capacity expansion is at AXT’s Beijing facility, precisely the jurisdiction where export licensing and materials controls have become a live issue.
>
> The deal is financially immaterial to COHR in isolation. COHR’s market cap is roughly $65B and the $22.3M prepayment is de minimis against the equity value, capex program, and cash balance. It is best viewed as a capacity reservation / working-capital deposit, likely recorded as a prepaid asset and then consumed through substrate purchases, not as an immediate P&L event. COHR was trading near $333 after a roughly -9.6% move on July 2, so the stock reaction is more likely to be driven by AI hardware sentiment, valuation, and semiconductor tape than by a $22M supplier prepayment.
>
> For AXTI, however, the signal is materially stronger. AXT reported Q1 2026 revenue of $26.9M, so a $22.3M prepayment is roughly 83% of a single quarter’s reported revenue, even though it is not immediately recognized as revenue and the total contract value could be meaningfully different from the prepayment. AXT also said in April that it had completed a $632.5M capital raise to support Tongmei’s InP capacity expansion and 6-inch InP R&D, so the COHR contract provides named strategic-customer validation for that capital deployment.   AXTI was down roughly -12.9% on July 2, and this after-close filing could support a rebound when regular trading resumes.
>
> The most important subtlety is that the $22.3M should not be treated as the total revenue opportunity. The filing says the prepayment is applied against purchases and ties to committed capacity; it does not disclose wafer volumes, per-wafer prices, shipment cadence, gross margin, or whether additional capacity is expected to be purchased beyond the initial commitment. Using Reuters’ cited $5,000 average 6-inch InP wafer price as a purely illustrative benchmark, the prepayment would equate to roughly 4,500 wafers, but that calculation should not be used as a volume estimate because actual contract pricing is confidential and the prepayment may only represent a portion of the broader commitment.  
>
> The fixed-price element is meaningful. If spot 6-inch InP pricing continues to rise, Coherent has partially hedged substrate cost and capacity access. That matters for the gross margin bridge because COHR’s >42% non-GAAP gross margin path relies on 6-inch cost/yield benefits, higher 1.6T mix, internal sourcing, and better absorption. J.P. Morgan’s May conference note highlighted 42%+ gross margin tailwinds from the shift from 800G to higher-margin 1.6T, the transition from 3-inch to 6-inch wafers, and movement from external to internal sourcing.   The AXT agreement supports that framework, but the benefit likely shows up gradually through wafer starts, device output, module shipments, and margin conversion rather than immediately in the next quarter.
>
> This is also a useful read-through to AI optical demand. Coherent is not just receiving long-term customer commitments; it is passing those commitments upstream. That is how a real supply-constrained hardware cycle behaves. Customers commit to COHR, COHR commits to AXT, AXT expands Beijing 6-inch capacity, and the entire chain becomes increasingly governed by deposits, capacity reservations, fixed prices, minimum orders, and termination protections. This reinforces the view that the AI optical cycle is capacity constrained rather than purely speculative order inflation, though it does not disprove some double-ordering risk.
>
> The agreement also has a China-risk wrinkle that investors should not ignore. Coherent has emphasized U.S. manufacturing scale, Sherman 6-inch InP leadership, CHIPS-related support, and the NVIDIA strategic partnership. This AXT agreement reveals that even a U.S.-anchored 6-inch InP device strategy still depends on upstream substrate inputs from China. That is not inherently negative, because AXT is a scaled and strategically important substrate supplier, but it means export permits, U.S.-China policy, force majeure language, and qualification of non-China supply remain critical diligence items.
>
> Relative implications are clear. For COHR, this is a positive data point for execution confidence and supply visibility, but not enough on its own to revise estimates. For AXTI, it is a much bigger validation event because it confirms that a leading AI optical platform company is willing to prepay for Tongmei 6-inch substrate capacity. For LITE, the read-through is mixed: positive for the industry because InP scarcity is validated, but potentially negative at the margin if COHR is locking a larger share of scarce AXT 6-inch output. For the broader optical ecosystem, the deal supports the view that the scarcity value sits not only in finished transceivers but also deep upstream in compound semiconductor substrates, lasers, isolators, PM fiber, ELS modules, and other enabling components.
>
> Trading implication: this should help stabilize the COHR narrative after the July 2 selloff, but it is not large enough to single-handedly re-rate the stock. The better near-term setup is probably AXTI up more sharply on customer validation and COHR modestly supported, with the caveat that U.S. markets are closed Friday, July 3 for Independence Day observed, so regular-session price discovery is delayed.   COHR remains a high-conviction structural AI optical beneficiary, but the stock still needs gross margin progression, 6-inch output conversion, and FCF inflection to justify the valuation. This announcement improves confidence in the supply-chain bridge to that outcome.
>
> Key diligence questions for Monday/next week: whether this AXT capacity was already included in COHR’s “5 substrate suppliers” commentary or is incremental; whether export licenses are already secured; what share of FY2027 6-inch wafer starts this covers; whether the agreement includes first-priority capacity rights or merely committed capacity; whether the fixed wafer prices are below current spot; how quickly AXT can qualify volume 6-inch wafers to COHR specifications; and whether any of the prepayment is ultimately customer-funded through COHR’s own strategic LTAs.

> $sive ⚡️
>
> Sivers Semiconductors ($SIVE) is a deep-tech company that designs and manufactures specialized microchips and lasers for ultra-fast, high-capacity communications.
>
> Instead of using traditional electrical copper wiring—which creates heat and becomes a bottleneck at high speeds—Sivers builds high-power lasers and laser arrays that transmit data using light (silicon photonics).
>
> While Photonics is the AI growth engine Sivers also designs radio frequency integrated circuits (RFICs) and beamforming antennas that operate on millimeter-wave (mmWave) frequencies.
>
> Under 2b Market Cap this is a high risk and highly speculative play.  Current revenues/contracts and assest in no way make the current valuation.  Much of the valuation is still derived from a "potential pipeline" and "potential opportunity" but the potential upside is immense if they can execute.

> •Sector-wide component: growth/photonics multiple compression hitting AAOI, COHR, LITE simultaneously — this is macro/rotation, not fundamental to SIVE.

> $ALMU $ALMU continues building the team needed to move from R&D to commercial production.
>
> The company appointed Brendan Moran, Ph.D. as Vice President of Engineering, a key hire as Aeluma prepares to scale manufacturing of its compound semiconductor technology.
>
> Moran brings 18 years at Lumileds, where he led product strategy and development for a mobile flash business generating over $300 million in annual revenue. He also oversaw the launch of 25+ products into high-volume manufacturing, producing more than 4 billion semiconductor devices, and managed engineering teams responsible for taking products from development to mass production.
>
> Why this matters:
>
> Developing breakthrough semiconductor technology is only half the challenge. The harder part is turning lab-scale innovation into reliable, high-volume manufacturing that customers can deploy. That’s exactly where Moran’s experience fits.
>
> For Aeluma, the focus is now shifting from proving its technology to commercializing it across AI infrastructure, optical communications, defense, aerospace, quantum computing, AR/VR, automotive and advanced sensing.
>
> Aeluma’s platform integrates high-performance compound semiconductors with standard silicon manufacturing, aiming to deliver the performance advantages of III-V materials while using scalable semiconductor production processes. If successful, this could lower manufacturing costs while enabling broader adoption in fast-growing AI and photonics markets.
>
> For investors, this is more than a management hire. It’s another signal that Aeluma is preparing for its next phase—moving beyond R&D and positioning itself for commercial revenue, manufacturing scale, and customer deployment.

### Rahul Sondhi (@oajuo27267451)
_Tue Jun 30 17:59:46 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 8 · ↻ 1 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/oajuo27267451/status/2072017264489164868)

> $SIVE is being mispriced because the market is still reading it as a small photonics hardware vendor.
>
> That framing is outdated.
>
> The real position is inside the AI optical stack, at a specific constraint layer: the laser source.
>
> AI networking stack is shifting fast:
>
> GPU clusters
> → scale-out bandwidth demand
> → 800G to 1.6T optics transition
> → CPO / LPO architecture shift
> → laser source layer becomes the constraint
> → InP / EML / CW laser ecosystem
>
> Sivers sits in that lower layer.
>
> Not as a module assembler.
>
> But closer to the optical source and integration bottleneck that determines whether higher-level optics can actually scale.
>
> The key shift the market is missing:
>
> AI is no longer primarily a compute scaling problem.
>
> It is becoming a data movement problem.
>
> And data movement is limited by optical physics, not silicon performance.
>
> Three structural points:
>
> First, bandwidth demand in AI clusters is accelerating faster than electrical interconnect scaling.
>
> Second, 1.6T and CPO architectures increase dependency on stable, high-quality laser sources.
>
> Third, once optical components are designed into a platform, replacement cycles are long and sticky.
>
> This changes how SIVE should be viewed.
>
> Not as a cyclical supplier tied to component demand.
>
> But as a potential design-in layer in optical reference architectures.
>
> The bull case is not near-term revenue growth.
>
> It is architectural adoption.
>
> If Sivers becomes embedded in next-generation optical designs, demand becomes structural across hyperscaler buildouts.
>
> Risks remain significant:
>
> early-stage business model
> historical dilution
> customer concentration
> execution risk in scaling photonics manufacturing
>
> This is still a high-volatility setup.
>
> But the key re-rating driver is simple:
>
> Control points in AI systems are shifting from compute to connectivity, and from connectivity to optical physics.
>
> That is where Sivers sits.@aleabitoreddit 
> #StockMarket  #Investing

### FairMarketWatch (@FairMarketWatch)
_Tue Jun 30 18:23:50 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/FairMarketWatch/status/2072023321290383637)

> 💰 Nyemissioner - positivt eller negativt? Allt handlar om syftet.
>
> Jag har märkt att många småsparare och nya investerare automatiskt kopplar ordet nyemission till något negativt och därför blir oroliga.
>
> Det är fullt förståeligt – många nyemissioner genomförs när bolag har ekonomiska problem.
>
> Men det betyder inte att alla nyemissioner ser likadana ut. I detta fallet handlar det dessutom om en riktad nyemission som riktas direkt mot större institutionella investerare och kommer dessutom genomföras över natten.
>
> ⸻
>
> I Sivers, $SIVE, fall är budskapet från bolaget tydligt:
>
> Kapitalet ska användas för att öka kapaciteten och möta en växande efterfrågan inom flera av bolagets viktigaste affärsområden, bland annat:
>
> ✅ Optiska lasrar och optiska förstärkare för AI-datacenter
>
> ✅ Automotive LiDAR
>
> ✅ Fortsatt expansion inom Photonics
>
> Bolaget beskriver alltså inte en situation där kapitalet behövs för att hålla verksamheten vid liv, utan för att kunna genomföra nästa tillväxtfas. Det är en viktig skillnad!
>
> ⸻
>
> Om kapitalet används för att öka produktionskapaciteten, möta en växande efterfrågan och skapa högre framtida intäkter kan värdet på bolaget över tid utvecklas positivt trots att antalet aktier ökar.
>
> Det är just därför syftet med en nyemission är minst lika viktigt som nyemissionen i sig.
>
> ⸻
>
> Det är också värt att komma ihåg att Sivers under det senaste året kommunicerat:
>
> 🔹 En växande pipeline inom AI-datacenter.
>
> 🔹 Produktionsupptrappning inom Automotive LiDAR från H2 2026.
>
> 🔹 Flera planerade produktionsramper under 2026–2027.
>
> Det är mot den bakgrunden jag tycker att den här nyemissionen ska bedömas.
>
> Personligen ser jag denna nyemissionen har ett väldigt starkt signalvärde kring vart bolaget är på väg!
>
> ⸻
>
> Detta är inte en köp- eller säljrekommendation.
>
> Jag tycker bara att det är viktigt att läsa hela pressmeddelandet och förstå varför bolaget tar in kapital – inte bara reagera på ordet nyemission!

### Rahul Sondhi (@Sondhi245)
_Tue Jun 30 18:40:46 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/Sondhi245/status/2072027581759840411)

> Thread
>
> Everyone keeps asking the same question.
>
> "Which company wins AI?" 
> $NVDA $AVGO $AMD $TSM $MU $MSFT $GOOGL $AMZN $META $ORCL $PLTR ?
>
> I think that's the wrong question.
>
> The better question is:
>
> Which company becomes impossible to replace?
>
> The AI infrastructure buildout isn't being constrained by GPUs anymore.
>
> It's becoming constrained by everything around them.
>
> Power.
>
> Cooling.
>
> Memory.
>
> Networking.
>
> And increasingly...
>
> Light.
>
> Most investors still think optical networking is about transceivers.
>
> It isn't.
>
> The real value is quietly moving upstream.
>
> Every new optical architecture—whether it's pluggables, Scale-Out CPO, Scale-Up CPO, Near-Packaged Optics, or External Laser Source (ELS)—still depends on one thing:
>
> A stable, high-volume CW laser.
>
> Different architectures.
>
> Same dependency.
>
> That's where supply-chain mapping becomes interesting.
>
> This is why I continue spending far more time studying suppliers than hyperscalers.
>
> Hyperscalers change vendors.
>
> Platforms evolve.
>
> Chip architectures change.
>
> But infrastructure bottlenecks?
>
> Those usually last much longer than people expect.
>
> The companies solving those bottlenecks often capture the highest operating leverage of the entire cycle.
>
> This is exactly why I find $SIVE so interesting.
>
> Most people still describe Sivers as "a laser company."
>
> I think that's missing the point.
>
> The product isn't the thesis.
>
> Its position in the supply chain is.
>
> If multiple AI networking architectures all require the same laser technology, then the value isn't coming from any single customer.
>
> It's coming from becoming embedded across the ecosystem.
>
> That's a completely different investment framework.
>
> People also underestimate how infrastructure cycles actually work.
>
> Revenue is always the last thing to arrive.
>
> First comes R&D.
>
> Then qualification.
>
> Then design wins.
>
> Then ecosystem validation.
>
> Only after all of that do production ramps begin.
>
> Investors waiting for obvious revenue growth are usually arriving after the market has already repriced the opportunity.
>
> One thing I think the market still misunderstands is timing.
>
> Many investors expect AI photonics to become a meaningful revenue driver this quarter.
>
> I don't.
>
> The real story is what happens when next-generation optical deployments begin scaling throughout 2027.
>
> That's when supply-chain positioning starts to matter far more than quarterly headlines.
>
> I've said this before:
>
> I don't invest by asking,
>
> "Who sells the most AI chips?"
>
> I ask,
>
> "Who does everyone else quietly depend on?"
>
> Those companies rarely make headlines.
>
> But they often become the biggest winners of the cycle.
>
> That's why I continue mapping bottlenecks instead of narratives.
>
> NFA. DYODD.@aleabitoreddit #StockMarket  #Investing #AI

### Investor Denis (@InvestorDenis)
_Tue Jun 30 19:05:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 45 · ↻ 5 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/InvestorDenis/status/2072033679514468359)

> $IONQ is looking to become vertically integrated.
>
> The acquisition of $SKYT seems like the missing piece.
>
> It’s not.
>
> $IONQ buys laser systems from Coherent and NKT Photonics.
>
> Coherent is a US company that supplies lasers to $IONQ called Coherent Paladin.
>
> The ultraviolet lasers produce light at specific wavelengths for the atomic transitions in barium and ytterbium that $IONQ uses.
>
> Those are standard benchtop setups for general qubit manipulation. They’re massive and require lab environment to operate.
>
> Then there’s NKT Photonics from Denmark. It supplies tailor made crystal fiber lasers with low noise. The goal here is to use the lasers in datacenters.
>
> The setup is smaller so that the lasers can be mounted in a 19-inch rack with the other components of the quantum computer.
>
> The lasers are ultra-stable and narrow-linewidth. It’s challenging to simply swap them with anyone else’s lasers.
>
> Which makes $IONQ vulnerable to this specific supply chain.
>
> Coherent relies on gallium, germanium, and rare-earth elements, most of which are mined in China. China suspended its total ban on exporting critical dual-use metals to the US until November 27, 2026.
>
> What will happen after? Nobody knows.
>
> We know from Coherent’s 2023 update that it had ample inventories and suppliers outside of China.
>
> NKT Photonics sources nonlinear crystals used to build frequency converters from Europe, Japan, and the US.
>
> The dangers here are regulations and delays.
>
> NKT Photonics is a subsidiary of Hamamatsu Photonics. It has preferential access to Hamamatsu’s supply chain of laser diodes and optical components.
>
> Trade wars between Europe and Japan are unlikely, but if they happen, NKT Photonics will be affected.
>
> Finally, its lasers are dual use: They can be used in quantum computers and military guidance or radar systems.
>
> Any sudden restrictions by Danish authorities could result in bottlenecks.
>
> $IONQ is managing its supply chain nicely but dangers remain.

### Alex (@chjkfddd20703)
_Tue Jun 30 19:31:29 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 29 · ↻ 11 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/chjkfddd20703/status/2072040346771763622)

> Russia ITMO University: Optical Tractor Beam with Metasurfaces and United States: Boeing's Magnetic Tractor Beam Patent
>
> #ufotwitter
>
> It's fascinating milestone in the field of modern nanophotonics. Published in ACS Photonics in late 2018 by physicists from ITMO University, the research details how hyperbolic metasurfaces can be used to generate stable optical pulling forces—commonly referred to as an "optical tractor beam."
>
> To understand how this functions, it helps to look at the mechanics of standard radiation pressure and contrast it with how these specialized, engineered surfaces flip that mechanic on its head.
>
> The Problem with Normal Light
>
> Under ordinary conditions, when a laser beam strikes a small dielectric particle, the photons transfer their linear momentum to the object. This creates a standard scattering or radiation pressure that pushes the particle away from the light source, along the direction of propagation.
>
> Creating a "tractor beam" requires generating a negative optical force (a pulling force) that acts against the global momentum of the incoming light, drawing the particle backward toward the source.
>
> How Hyperbolic Metasurfaces Change the Mechanics
>
> A hyperbolic metasurface is an ultra-thin, artificially engineered material characterized by extreme anisotropy. This means its electromagnetic properties (specifically its permittivity, have different signs along different spatial axes—for example, acting like a metal  in one direction and like a dielectric in another.
>
> When a small particle is placed close to this surface and illuminated by a standard unstructured light source (like a plane wave), the interaction relies on three core phenomena:
>
> High Density of States & Asymmetric Scattering: The hyperbolic nature of the substrate opens up highly localized, high-density electromagnetic interaction channels (both surface plasmons and volumetric waves within the substrate). The presence of the particle scatterer near the interface selectively excites these asymmetrical near-field modes.
>
> Momentum Conservation and Recoil: Because the substrate allows light to scatter preferentially into these highly confined, high-momentum modes directed forward along or into the surface, the law of conservation of linear momentum requires a balance. To compensate for the forward momentum of the tailored scattering channels, the particle experiences a net mechanical recoil in the opposite direction.
>
> Broadband Pulling: Unlike older optical trapping configurations that require complex, actively modulated phase holograms or spatial light modulators (SLMs) to sculpt a specific beam geometry (like a solenoid or Bessel beam), this model utilizes the intrinsic dispersion of the substrate itself. This allows for stable optical pulling forces over a significantly broader spectral range using simpler incident light fields.
>
> Why This Mattered
>
> Prior to this approach, pulling particles with light required highly complex, bulky optical setups that restricted spatial movement and demanded high laser power, which could damage biological samples or nanoscale structures. By shifting the engineering challenge from the light source to the material environment (the metasurface), this framework opened up new avenues for nanoscale manipulation, chip-based sorting of cells or macromolecules, and nanoscale fluidic self-organization.
>
> United States: Boeing's Magnetic Tractor Beam Patent
>
> This is an interesting find. You’re looking at US Patent US6634603B2, titled "Magnetic dipole tractor beam control system", filed by The Boeing Company back in 2001 and granted in 2003.
>
> While the phrase "tractor beam" instantly evokes sci-fi, the actual engineering framework here is grounded in classic electromagnetic field manipulation. Here is a breakdown of what this patent actually describes, how it works, and its intended application.
>
> The Core Concept: How It Works
>
> Unlike fictional tractor beams that use exotic energy to pull objects across massive distances, this system relies on the predictable physics of magnetic dipole interactions.
>
> If you have two magnetic dipoles (which can be generated using electromagnets or superconducting loops), they exert a force and a torque on one another based on their relative orientation, distance, and field strength.
>
> The patent describes a system designed to:
>
> Attract or Repel: Manipulate the magnetic fields to pull a target object closer or push it away.
>
> Control Orientation: Adjust the torque to precisely rotate, stabilize, or align the target object in three-dimensional space without physical contact.
>
> Dynamic Feedback: Continuously measure the position and orientation of the target, feeding that data into a control processor to adjust the magnetic fields in real-time, preventing the target from drifting or snapping violently out of position.
>
> The Intended Application
>
> In space, docking two multi-ton vehicles (like a shuttle or capsule connecting to a space station) is incredibly risky. Mechanical docking mechanisms require physical impact, which can transmit dangerous kinetic energy, cause structural fatigue, or send both craft into an uncontrolled tumble if misaligned.
>
> The "Tractor Beam" Solution:
>
> By using this magnetic dipole control system, a chaser spacecraft could:
>
> Approach a passive target satellite or station module.
>
> Activate the controlled magnetic fields from a safe distance.
>
> Gently capture, damp out any residual spin (tumble) of the target, and guide it into a precise mechanical lock without ever touching it until the final capture.
>
> It's a highly sophisticated, non-contact magnetic tethering and dampening system—essentially a high-tech "soft-capture" mechanism for orbital logistics.
>
> https://t.co/SVyihryf3Z
> https://t.co/397pKmkCbR

### charahim94 (@charahim9494)
_Tue Jun 30 19:59:54 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 3 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/charahim9494/status/2072047497930047972)

> This 🎯roadmap🎯 for data-center interconnect speeds is also, in many ways, a roadmap for #siliconphotonics.  As data rates move higher, the industry will need more integrated optical solutions, including near-package optics and co-packaged optics. That is where #siliconphotonics becomes increasingly relevant.
> I adapted this roadmap based on analysis from an investment bank, which states that it is built on company disclosures as well as its own research.
> It is interesting to observe how the upgrade cycles are overlapping. According to this analysis 400G is already moving into decline, 800G is becoming the mainstream workhorse, 1.6T is entering mass-volume territory, and 3.2T is already visible before 1.6T has fully settled. Furthermore, 800G may remain mainstream for only around six quarters. That is shorter than the typical 2–4 year cadence often expected for a mainstream optical transceiver generation. This points to a compressed innovation cadence for the industry. Qualification, yield learning, supply-chain readiness, thermal design, packaging, DSP, and test infrastructure all need to mature faster than before. Only the 💪fittest can survive this race. My view is that integrated photonics is entering a sustained innovation cycle, driven by the bandwidth, power, density, and packaging pressures of AI data-center infrastructure. 
> 🚀 #siliconphotonics

### Joey Zhuo (@JoeyZhuo777)
_Tue Jun 30 20:03:45 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/JoeyZhuo777/status/2072048464947478850)

> Here's the post:
>
> If I could only watch four layers in optical interconnect, ranked by bottleneck severity:
> $COHR $LITE $FN $ANET
>
> Nvidia just spent $6 billion locking down optical supply between March and June, and the market still thinks this is about transceivers.
>
> The real story is InP substrates and laser chips — the stuff 20 layers upstream from what most people are tracking. Here's how I'd rank the supply chain by choke point plus earnings visibility over the next 12-24 months.
>
> 1. InP materials and epitaxy — the actual valve on compute scale. $COHR and $LITE aren't just CPO plays. They control high-purity indium phosphide epitaxy and high-speed laser IP that physically cannot be replaced in 800G/1.6T modules. Intel's CEO said it outright: InP is the non-negotiable material for solving chip-to-chip bandwidth. Nvidia locked each of them with separate $2 billion commitments and long-term offtake agreements. The Street prices them as module vendors. They're actually material oligopolists with compounding pricing power through every speed iteration.
>
> 2. CPO laser engines — the leverage on every GPU watt. $LITE and $COHR again, but now wearing their co-packaged optics hat. CPO moves the photonics inside the package, right next to the switch ASIC or GPU. That requires advanced packaging plus high-power lasers that don't cook themselves. Supply is sewn up. Goldman just put the scale-up interconnect TAM at $154 billion, and most of that growth is inside the rack and inside the super-pod, not between data centers. CPO sits in the middle of that build-out. Earnings inflection is 2026-2028 when hyperscalers move from pilots to volume. Risk is simple: if Nvidia capex wobbles, these names will gap hard because the trade is already crowded.
>
> 3. Module assembly and high-mix manufacturing — where cash flow actually prints. $FN is the TSMC of optical: low-drama contract manufacturing for every major module and CPO vendor. Margins are thinner than the chip guys, but revenue visibility is the cleanest in the whole chain because hyperscale deployment schedules are locked 18 months out. TrendForce just lifted 2025-2026 AI transceiver revenue from $16.5 billion to $26 billion, up 57% year-over-year. FN captures that with zero demand risk and no inventory. It's the only name here where you can model the next eight quarters with a straight face.
>
> 4. Switch and networking integration — the layer everyone already owns. $ANET is the consensus optical AI trade. Data center switching tied to optical back-end is a known quantity. Multiples reflect it. I'd rather own the three above because the market hasn't priced the material and assembly bottleneck the same way it's priced the switch attach rate.
>
> The non-consensus bit: A-share money has been rotating from NAND and legacy semis into InP names for two quarters, but U.S. allocators still think optical is a 2025 story. It's a 2026-2028 margin story, and the earnings gap between upstream material plays and downstream module integrators is about to widen hard. I'm overweight the top two on that list until CPO production data forces multiple expansion.

### ZPF (@zpfTechnologies)
_Tue Jun 30 21:00:06 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 50 · ↻ 16 · 💬 7 · [open on X](https://x.com/zpfTechnologies/status/2072062644534538538)

> https://t.co/0ncKgB2wBv
>
> This is exactly the kind of experiment more people should be paying attention to.
>
> Scientists used water waves to make an otherwise “invisible” quantum-style effect visible. A vortex in a tank acted as an analogue to the magnetic-flux structure in the Aharonov–Bohm effect. The waves did not need to pass through the vortex core for the global wave pattern to change.
>
> That is the key point.
>
> A hidden topological structure altered the phase of the wave environment, and the result became visible as system-wide nodal lines. Even more interesting: as the vortex strength increased, the number of rotating nodal lines became quantized.
>
> To me, the deeper lesson is not “water proves quantum mechanics.”
>
> It is that organized wave environments can reveal invisible structure through global diagnostic patterns.
>
> Topology became visible.
>
> Phase became visible.
>
> A local organizing feature produced a non-local wave signature.
>
> That matters far beyond this one experiment.
>
> For ZPF Technologies, this is close to the language we are trying to formalize: dynamically organized electromagnetic environments should not only be analyzed by field strength or energy density. They should also be studied through phase, topology, boundary conditions, mode accessibility, noise structure, sidebands, linewidths, and residuals after standard explanations are subtracted.
>
> If water waves can reveal hidden topological structure through nodal patterns, then advanced electromagnetic systems deserve the same kind of diagnostic imagination.
>
> The frontier is not just building stronger fields.
>
> It is learning how organized environments leave organized observables.
>
> That is where topology, phase, stochastic dynamics, quantum vacuum diagnostics, photonics, plasma systems, and future fusion research may begin to converge.
> #Quantum #quantumphysics #QuantumEngineering

### パウロ (@paurooteri)
_Tue Jun 30 21:45:16 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 159 · ↻ 6 · 💬 6 · [open on X](https://x.com/paurooteri/status/2072074013409755187)

> テスト、テスト、テスト
>
> 価格上昇の件数は、ウェハー製造工場よりもさらに多く、AI、シリコンフォトニクス、成熟したチップのパッケージングとテストに関する受注は2027年まで続いている。
>
> クラウドベースのAIに対する需要の高まりは、半導体業界の季節的なパターンを塗り替えつつあります。製造工程の最終段階に位置するパッケージングおよびテスト能力は、2025年末以降、逼迫した状態が続いています。2026年以降、新たに拡張された能力は急速に活用され、多くのIC設計顧客が積極的に能力確保に乗り出し、2027年以降の受注見通しが向上しています。
>
> パッケージング用リードフレーム、IC基板、テスト用電気料金の同時増加に伴い、パッケージングおよびテストファウンドリサービスの価格上昇がここ数四半期で特に顕著になっていることは特筆に値する。価格上昇の回数で見ると、ウェハファウンドリを上回り、IC設計顧客にとって最大のコスト圧力源となっている。
>
> したがって、AIが半導体市場の本格的な回復を牽引するにつれ、高度なパッケージングおよびテストサービスと従来型のパッケージングおよびテストサービスの両方、ならびに上流工程のリードフレーム、IC基板、プローブカード、ソケットに対する需要は、2026年後半も引き続き堅調に推移すると予想される。
>
> チップのパッケージングとテストのサプライチェーン全体には、ASE Technology Holdingとその子会社であるSPIL、Powertech、STARS、Chipbond、ChipMOS、SIM Semiconductorなどの主要OSATメーカー、King Yuan Electronics、Hsin Chuan、Siliconware Precision Industriesなどの専門テスト会社、Ingenic Semiconductor、Wintek、Yung-Chi、Chunghwa Precision Test、Hanmin Testなどのテストインターフェース会社、Chieh Lin、Shun-Te、Chang-Techなどのリードフレームメーカー、Unimicron、Kinsus、Nan Ya PCB、Zhen Dingなどの主要基板メーカーが含まれます。
>
> 近年のパッケージングおよびテスト関連価格の上昇を振り返ると、最初の波はメモリ市場における新たなスーパーサイクルであり、顧客はPowertechやChipMOSといったメモリパッケージングおよびテスト企業に緊急発注を行った。最初の価格上昇は2025年後半に発表され、2回目の価格上昇のニュースは2026年初頭に浮上した。
>
> 一方、GPU、CPU、ASICといった先端プロセスチップの生産増加に加え、データセンター周辺のネットワークおよび産業制御アプリケーションに対する需要の高まりも、成熟プロセスチップの在庫補充を促している。ICパッケージングおよびテスト市場は2025年後半から供給不足の状態が続いており、それに伴い、ASE Technology Holding Co., Ltd.やSiliconware Precision Industries Co., Ltd.といった企業も徐々に価格引き上げに合意している。
>
> 現在、メモリとICのパッケージングおよびテスト能力は半導体サプライチェーンにおけるボトルネックの一つとなっており、台湾のパッケージングおよびテストファウンドリ業界は史上最大規模の設備投資拡大期を迎えている。特に、パッケージングおよびテスト企業は、拡張スピードを加速させるため、ここ数ヶ月で台湾の既存工場を次々と買収し、用地準備や工場建設にかかる時間を節約しており、業界からも大きな注目を集めている。
>
> さらに重要なことに、稼働準備が整ったパッケージング・テスト工場のすべての新工場と生産ラインは、顧客にとって重要な戦略的資源となっている。例えば、ChipMOSは、あるメモリ顧客が生産能力拡張のための設備投資を確保するため、同社と3年間の長期契約を締結したと述べている。また、Silicon Photonicsは、湖口第2工場のクリーンルーム改修プロジェクトが完了する前に、Silicon Photonicsの顧客が既に全生産能力を予約済みであると指摘している。

### Drew Ponder (@drew_ponder)
_Tue Jun 30 23:02:52 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 1 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/drew_ponder/status/2072093540394631219)

> Quantum computing’s disappearing use cases reveal what the money is really buying
>
> For years, quantum computing was promoted as the coming solution to drug discovery, logistics, finance, artificial intelligence, climate modeling, encryption, and nearly every difficult optimization problem. Yet as classical algorithms, GPUs, and specialized accelerators improved, many proposed quantum advantages became smaller, more conditional, or impossible to demonstrate on real hardware. DARPA’s Quantum Benchmarking Initiative now defines success as proving that a quantum computer’s computational value exceeds its operating cost, with the program attempting to determine whether such a utility-scale machine can be built by 2033. That is a revealing benchmark: useful quantum computing is still something being tested, not an established commercial reality. Despite this, announced public investment in quantum technology exceeded $10 billion in early 2025, while the U.S. Department of Energy later committed another $625 million to national quantum research centers.
>
> The investment continues because governments are not evaluating quantum technology like an ordinary consumer product. They are purchasing strategic insurance. Even a small probability of achieving superior cryptanalysis, molecular simulation, navigation, sensing, communications, or materials design could alter the military and economic balance between nations. NIST has already finalized post-quantum encryption standards and urged organizations to begin migrating immediately, even though the cryptographically relevant quantum computer those standards defend against does not yet exist. This means the quantum race is driven partly by a fear that being late would be catastrophic, while being early could produce enormous intelligence and technological advantages.
>
> The other explanation is that “quantum computing” has become an umbrella used to finance a much larger technological ecosystem. The money supports photonics, cryogenics, superconducting materials, precision lasers, atomic clocks, quantum sensors, control electronics, secure networks, fabrication methods, software, patents, and highly specialized scientific talent. A universal fault-tolerant computer could fail to arrive on schedule while these supporting technologies still become commercially or militarily valuable. Investors may therefore be buying the infrastructure surrounding quantum control rather than betting exclusively on a machine that replaces classical computers. The true assets are the laboratories, intellectual property, supply chains, personnel, and control systems required to manipulate matter at increasingly precise scales.
>
> Frequency Wave Theory offers a deeper interpretation: perhaps the shrinking list of conventional computing applications is happening because “computer” was never the complete description of the technology. Quantum machines are fundamentally devices for preparing, isolating, synchronizing, and measuring coherent states. Their essential achievement is not merely calculating faster, but controlling phase, interference, tunneling, entanglement, and environmental noise. From the Frequency Wave Theory perspective, investment keeps rising because governments and corporations are learning how to engineer reality at the frequency-and-phase level. Computation may be the public-facing justification, while the broader prize is programmable field control, producing new forms of sensing, communication, materials engineering, timing, energy manipulation, and eventually direct interaction with the deeper resonant structure of the vacuum.

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HMGOFrQaoAAo1Ox.jpg

### 게로밍 (@zsdcxa13)
_Tue Jun 30 23:46:04 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 12 · ↻ 2 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/zsdcxa13/status/2072104411393077438)

> 앞으로 엔비디아 주가나 반도체 패권을 결정할 진짜 무기는 GPU가 아니라 '빛'일지도 모릅니다.
>
>  최근 엔비디아가 왜 구리선 대신 반도체 칩 안에 '레이저(빛)'를 집어넣는 기술에만 무려 65억 달러(9조 원) 넘는 돈을 쏟아부었을까요?
>
>  반도체 판을 통째로 바꿀 '빛의 속도' 전쟁
>
> 지금 반도체 공학자들이 마주한 가장 큰 벽은 의외로 연산 속도가 아닙니다. 
>
> 바로 우리가 늘 쓰는 '구리선(전기 신호)'의 물리적 한계예요.
>
> 지금까지 칩과 칩은 구리선으로 데이터를 주고받았는데, 
>
> AI 시대가 오면서 데이터가 폭발하니까 구리선이 버티질 못하는 상황이 온 거죠.
>
> 전기를 너무 많이, 빠르게 흘리니까 불타오르듯 열이 나고(발열), 전기 신호가 구리선 중심이 아니라 '겉표면'으로만 흐르려고 해서 속도가 뚝 떨어지는 병목 현상이 생깁니다.
>
> 쉽게 말해 경부고속도로에 갑자기 수백만 대의 슈퍼카가 몰려와서 도로 전체가 주차장으로 변하고 엔진이 과열되는 상태인 거죠.
>
> "야, 이대로 가다간 데이터센터 전기세 감당도 안 되고 칩이 다 타 죽겠다!" 
>
> 그래서 나온 천재적인 치트키가 바로 '실리콘 포토닉스(Silicon Photonics)'입니다.
>
> 쉽게 말해, 
>
> 우리가 국가 간 인터넷 연결할 때 쓰는 거대한 '광케이블'을 아주 미세하게 축소해서 반도체 칩 안에 통째로 집어넣는 기술이에요. 
>
> 전기가 아니라 빛으로 대화하는 칩인 셈이죠.
>
> 이게 왜 대박이냐면, 구리선은 선 하나당 신호 하나만 갈 수 있잖아요? 
>
> 근데 빛은 '색상(파장)'만 다르면 하나의 통로에서 수십 개의 신호가 섞이지 않고 동시에 달릴 수 있어요.
>
> 길을 물리적으로 넓히지 않아도 차선이 무한대로 늘어나는 마법 같은 효과가 생기는 겁니다. 속도가 수십 배 뛰는 건 당연하고요.
>
> 게다가 빛은 마찰열(저항)이 아예 없습니다. 
>
> AI 데이터센터에서 가장 골치 아픈 '발열'과 이를 식히기 위한 '냉각 비용'을 최대 30~40%까지 날려버릴 수 있다는 뜻이죠.
>
> 실제로 엔비디아가 올해(2026년) 들어서만
>
>  코히어런트, 루멘텀 같은 광학·유리 소재 기업들에 조 단위 투자를 감행한 이유가 여기 있습니다. 
>
> 구리선으로는 수백만 대의 GPU를 하나로 묶는 게 불가능하다는 걸 알기 때문이죠.
>
> 그럼 이 엄청난 칩은 대체 누가 만들까요?
>
>  결국 파운드리와 패키징 싸움입니다.
>
> TSMC는 전기 칩 위에 광학 칩을 아파트처럼 수직으로 완벽하게 쌓아 올리는 'COUPE'라는 자체 플랫폼을 만들어서 올해 본격적인 양산 카운트다운에 들어갔습니다. 
>
> 반도체 제조의 중심축이 미세 공정을 넘어 '광학 패키징'으로 이동하고 있는 국면이에요.
>
> 요약하자면, 
>
> HBM 다음 타자로 반도체 시장의 판돈을 싹 쓸어 담을 핵심 키워드는 '실리콘 포토닉스'입니다. 
>
> 엔비디아의 독주를 막으려는 빅테크나, 이를 추격하는 파운드리 기업들에게는 절대 놓칠 수 없는 마지막 열쇠인 셈이죠.
>
> 앞으로 반도체 뉴스 보실 때 '광학', 'CPO', '실리콘 포토닉스'라는 단어가 보이면 무조건 주목해 보세요.
